and hung in plain view in a conspicuous place on the licensed premises.
   C.   Display Of Birth Defects Warning Signs:
      1.   Every holder of a retail license, whether the licensee sells or
offers for sale alcoholic liquors for use or consumption on or off the retail
license premises, shall cause a sign with the message "GOVERNMENT WARNING:
ACCORDING TO THE SURGEON GENERAL, WOMEN SHOULD NOT DRINK ALCOHOLIC BEVERAGES
DURING PREGNANCY BECAUSE OF THE RISK OF BIRTH DEFECTS" to be framed and hung in
plain view. These signs shall be no larger than eight and one- half inches by
eleven inches (81/2" x 11").
      2.   In the event there is no warning sign posted on the retailer's
premises, it shall be the responsibility of the Illinois Liquor Control
Commission to furnish the retailer with a warning sign. The retailer shall have
thirty (30) days from receipt of the warning sign to post it on the licensed
premises. Thereafter, a retailer who violates this subsection is subject to a
written warning for the first violation. For a second or subsequent violation,
the retailer shall pay a fine of at least twenty dollars ($20.00) but not more
than one hundred dollars ($100.00) for each such violation. For the third and
subsequent violations, each day the activity continues shall be a separate
violation.
   D.   Nontransferability Of License:
      1.   A license issued under this chapter shall be purely a personal
privilege, good for not to exceed twelve (12) months after issued, unless
sooner revoked as in this chapter authorized and provided, and shall not
constitute property, nor shall it be subject to attachment, garnishment or
execution, nor shall it be alienable or transferable, voluntarily or
involuntarily, or subject to being encumbered or hypothecated.
      2.   Such license shall not descend by the laws of testate or intestate
devolution, but it shall cease upon the death of the licensee; provided, that
executors and administrators of any estate of the deceased licensee and the
trustees of any insolvent or bankrupt licensee, when such estate consists in
part of alcoholic liquor, may continue the business of the sale of alcoholic
liquor under the order of the court having jurisdiction of such estate and may
exercise the privileges of such deceased, insolvent or bankrupt licensee, after
the death of such decedent, or such insolvency or bankruptcy, until the
expiration of such license, but not longer than six (6) months after the death,
bankruptcy or insolvency of such licensee. (Ord. 1529, 8-1-2017)
3-2-11: LOCATION AND PREMISES REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   Prohibited Locations:
      1.   No license shall be issued for the sale at retail of any alcoholic
liquor within one hundred feet (100') of any church, school, hospital, home for
aged or indigent persons or for veterans, their spouses or children or any
military or naval station; provided, that this prohibition shall not apply to
hotels offering restaurant service, regularly organized clubs or to
restaurants, food shops or other places where the sale of alcoholic liquors is
not the principal business carried on, if such place of business so exempted
shall have been established for such purposes prior to the taking effect of
this chapter; nor to the renewal of a license for the sale at retail of
alcoholic liquor on premises within one hundred feet (100') of any church or
school where such church or school has been established within such one hundred
feet (100') since the issuance of the original license. In the case of a
church, the distance of one hundred feet (100') shall be measured to the
nearest part of any buildings used for worship services or educational programs
and not to property boundaries.
      2.   Nothing in this subsection shall prohibit the issuance of a license
to a church or private school to sell, at retail, alcoholic liquor if any such
sales are limited to periods when groups are assembled on the premises solely
for the promotion of some common object other than the sale or consumption of
alcoholic liquors.
   B.   Change Of Location: A retail liquor dealer's license shall permit the
sale of alcoholic liquor only on the premises described in the application and
license. Such location may be changed only upon the written permit to make such
change issued by the Local Liquor Control Commissioner. No change of location
shall be permitted unless the proposed new location is a proper one for the
retail sale of alcoholic liquor under the law of the State and this Code.
   C.   Lighting: All licensed premises are required to have, at a minimum,
five (5) foot-candles of light at a distance of thirty inches (30") from the
floor in all public areas of the premises.
   D.   Outdoor Seating Areas - Restaurants: Any restaurant serving alcoholic
liquor in outdoor areas on the premises shall cause said outdoor area to be
completely enclosed with a fence at least six feet (6') high as approved by the
Liquor Commissioner having at least one emergency exit. (Ord. 1529, 8-1-2017)
3-2-12: SANITARY CONDITIONS:
   A.   Health Permit: Every licensee shall have, at all times, a valid
operating permit from the County Health Department, which regulates health
standards.
   B.   Sanitary Premises: All premises used for the retail sale of alcoholic
liquor, or for the storage of such liquor for such sale, shall be kept in a
clean and sanitary condition, and shall be kept in full compliance with the
codes regulating the condition of premises used for the storage or sale of food
for human consumption.
   C.   Diseased Employees: It shall be unlawful to employ in any premises used
for the retail sale of alcoholic liquor, any person who is afflicted with or
who is a carrier of any contagious, infectious or venereal disease, and it
shall be unlawful for any person who is afflicted with or a carrier of any such
disease to work in or about any premises or to engage in any way in the
handling, preparation or distribution of such liquor. (Ord. 1529, 8-1-2017)
3-2-13: UNDERAGE PERSONS:
   A.   Employment: It shall be unlawful for any person under the age of twenty
one (21) years to attend any bar or to draw, pour, or mix any alcoholic liquor
in any licensed retail premises. However, any person who is eighteen (18) years
of age or older may deliver alcoholic liquor to the patrons of a restaurant.
   B.   Procuring Liquor For: No person, after purchasing or otherwise
obtaining alcoholic liquor, shall sell, give or deliver such alcoholic liquor
to another person under the age of twenty one (21) years, except in the
performance of a religious ceremony or service.
   C.   Purchase Or Acceptance Of Liquor By; Possession Prohibited: Any person
to whom the sale, gift or delivery of any alcoholic liquor is prohibited
because of age shall not purchase or accept a gift of such alcoholic liquor, or
have such alcoholic liquor in his possession.
   D.   Notice Posted: In every licensed business where alcoholic liquor is
sold, there shall be displayed at all times in a prominent place, a printed
card which shall be supplied by the City Clerk, and which shall read as
follows:
YOU ARE SUBJECT TO A FINE UP TO $750.00 UNDER THE ORDINANCES OF THE CITY OF
CARMI IF YOU PURCHASE ALCOHOLIC LIQUOR, OR MISREPRESENT YOUR AGE FOR THE
PURPOSE OF PURCHASING OR OBTAINING ALCOHOLIC LIQUOR.
   E.   Presence On Licensed Premises: No person to whom the sale, gift or
delivery of any alcoholic liquor is prohibited because of age, either alone or
accompanied by an adult, shall enter or be suffered to remain in or on the
portion of licensed premises where alcoholic liquor is sold or any room or
place adjoining the same where alcoholic liquors are sold or served. Except
that minors may, if in the company of a parent or guardian, be permitted to
enter the dining or family room of the holder of a restaurant for the purpose
of eating and consuming food, provided the minor is seated at least ten feet
(10') from the nearest portion of the bar. With respect to Class F licenses, a
minor cannot enter the room where liquor is being mixed, poured, prepared or
sold, unless the licensee has upon application, obtained permission from the
Liquor Commission to allow minors, in the company of a parent or guardian, to
enter such room, while the licensee is hosting a reception, party, or similar
special event. Under no circumstances can a minor be served alcoholic liquor in
a dining or family room, or any other room on the licensed premises.
   F.   Identification Required: If a licensee or his agents or employees
believe or have reason to believe that a sale or delivery of any alcoholic
liquor is prohibited because of the age of the prospective recipient, he shall,
before making such sale or delivery, demand presentation of some form of
positive identification, containing proof of age, issued by a public officer in
the performance of his official duties. (Ord. 1529, 8-1-2017)
3-2-14: PROHIBITED ACTS AND CONDITIONS:
   A.   Sales To Certain Persons: No licensee, nor any officer, associate,
member, representative, agent or employee of such licensee, shall sell, give or
deliver alcoholic liquor to any person under the age of twenty one (21) years,
to any intoxicated person, or to any person known by him to be a habitual
drunkard, spendthrift, insane, mentally ill, mentally deficient, or in need of
mental treatment.
   B.   Removal Of Liquor From Premises:
      1.   It shall be unlawful for any person to remove, take, carry, convey
or transport from any licensed premises, any alcoholic liquor not in the
original, unopened package.
      2.   No licensee, his agents, servants or employees shall permit or allow
any person to remove, take, carry, convey or transport from the licensed
premises any alcoholic liquor except in the original, unopened package.
      3.   Any alcoholic liquor sold, bartered, exchanged, given, provided,
furnished or dispensed by any licensee, his agents, servants or employees, in
other than the original, unopened package, shall be used, consumed or otherwise
disposed of only upon the interior of such licensed premises.
      4.   No licensee, his agents, servants or employees shall sell, barter,
exchange, give, provide, furnish or dispense to any person any alcoholic liquor
for consumption or use in any place or location except the interior of the
licensed premises unless such alcoholic liquor shall be in the original,
unopened package.
   C.   Peddling Liquor: It shall be unlawful to peddle alcoholic liquor in the
City.
   D.   Disorderly Premises: A person licensed under this chapter shall not
suffer any disorder, drunkenness, quarreling, fighting, unlawful games, or
riotous or disorderly conduct in any licensed premises kept or occupied by him
for the sale of alcoholic liquor.
   E.   Nude Dancing: No licensee shall permit any form of nude dancing to take
place upon the licensed premises.
   F.   Gambling: No gambling shall be permitted and no gambling device shall
be kept in any premises licensed or permitted pursuant to this chapter. This
prohibition, however, shall not apply to any game or gaming event for which a
license or permit has been issued by the Illinois Department of Revenue
pursuant to the Pull Tabs and Jar Games Act, 230 Illinois Compiled Statutes 20/
1 et seq., the Bingo License and Tax Act, 230 Illinois Compiled Statutes 25/
1 et seq., the Illinois Video Gaming Act, 230 Illinois Compiled Statutes 40/
1 et seq., or the Charitable Games Act, 230 Illinois Compiled Statutes 30/1 et
seq., so long as such game or gaming event is conducted in compliance with all
requirements of said Acts and all rules and regulations of the Illinois
Department of Revenue.
   G.   Liquor In Automobiles: No person shall transport, carry, possess or
have any alcoholic liquor in or upon or about any motor vehicle except in the
original package and with the seal unbroken. (Ord. 1529, 8-1-2017)
3-2-15: RECORDS KEPT; NOTICE OF NEW LICENSES:
The Local Liquor Control Commissioner shall keep or cause to be kept, a
complete record of all licenses issued by him, and shall furnish the Clerk,
Treasurer and Chief of Police each with a copy thereof. Upon the issuance of
any new license, or the revocation of any old license, the Local Liquor Control
Commissioner shall give written notice of such action to each of these officers
within forty eight (48) hours of such action. (Ord. 1529, 8-1-2017)
3-2-16: VIOLATIONS; PENALTIES:
   A.   Liability For Violations:
      1.   If the owner of the licensed premises or any person from whom the
licensee derives the right to possession of such premises, or the agent of such
owner, or other person shall knowingly permit the licensee to use said licensed
premises in violation of the terms of this chapter, said owner, agent or other
person shall be deemed guilty of a violation of this chapter to the same extent
as said licensee and be subject to the same punishment.
      2.   Every act or omission of whatever nature constituting a violation of
the provisions of this chapter, by any officer, director, manager or other
agent or employee of any licensee, shall be deemed and held to be the act of
such employer or licensee, and said employer or licensee shall be punishable in
the same manner as if said act or omission had been done or omitted by him
personally.
   B.   Suspension Or Revocation Of License:
      1.   Upon violation by any licensee of any provision herein, the Local
Liquor Control Commissioner shall have power to suspend for not more than
thirty (30) days or revoke all local licenses issued to persons for premises
within the City.
      2.   Whenever any licensee shall be convicted of any violation of this
chapter, the license of said licensee may, in the discretion of the Local
Commissioner, be revoked and forfeited, and all fees paid thereon shall be
forfeited, and it shall thereafter be unlawful and shall constitute a further
violation of this chapter for said licensee to continue to operate under said
license.
   C.   Penalties For Underage Persons:
      1.   Any person under the age of twenty one (21) years, who purchases or
obtains any alcoholic liquor in any tavern, drugstore, or other place in the
City, where alcoholic liquor is sold, shall, upon conviction thereof, be
subject to a fine as provided in section
1-4-1 of this Code for each and every such offense.
      2.   Any person under the age of twenty one (21) years, who misrepresents
his or her age for the purpose of purchasing or obtaining alcoholic liquor in
any tavern, drugstore, or other place in the City where alcoholic liquor is
sold, shall, upon conviction thereof, be subject to a fine as provided in
section
1-4-1 of this Code for each and every such offense.
   D.   Penalty For Peddling: Any person who sells any alcoholic liquor
described in this chapter, without compliance with this chapter, shall, upon
conviction thereof, be subject to a fine as provided in section
1-4-1 of this Code.
   E.   Penalties For Broken Seals:
      1.   Broken Seals In Public: Any person who removes, takes, carries,
conveys or transports from any licensed premises, any alcoholic liquor not in
the original, unopened package, shall, upon conviction thereof, be subject to a
fine as provided in section
1-4-1 of this Code.
      2.   Broken Seal In Automobile: Any person who transports, carries,
possesses or has any alcoholic liquor in or upon or about any motor vehicle,
except in the original package and with the seal unbroken, shall, upon
conviction thereof, be subject to a fine as provided in section
1-4-1 of this Code.
   F.   Penalties For Drunken Or Intoxicated Condition Or Drinking Alcohol On
Streets, Alleys Or Sidewalks: It shall be unlawful for any person to be or
appear in a drunken or intoxicated condition or drink alcoholic liquor on the
streets, in the alleys, or on sidewalks or areas immediately adjacent thereto.
Any person who is in a drunken or intoxicated condition, or is drinking
alcoholic liquor on the streets, in the alleys, or sidewalks or areas
immediately adjacent thereto shall, upon conviction, be subject to a fine as
provided in section
1-4-1 of this Code. (Ord. 1529, 8-1-2017)
CHAPTER 3
COIN OPERATED AMUSEMENT DEVICES
SECTION:
3-3-1: Definitions
3-3-2: License Required
3-3-3: Application For License; Investigation And Approval
3-3-4: License Fees
3-3-5: Term Of License; Disposition Of Fees
3-3-6: Gambling
3-3-7: Violation; Penalty
3-3-1: DEFINITIONS:
Unless the context otherwise requires, the words and phrases herein defined are
used in this chapter in the sense given them in the following definitions:
COIN OPERATED AMUSEMENT DEVICE: Consists of any pool table, pinball machine or
video games where a person must insert one or more coins or other forms of
money, or tokens, in order to play or participate in a game offered by the pool
table, pinball or video game, including, but not limited to, any pool table,
pinball machine or video game where the players or participants pay a fee to
play or participate in a game offered by the pool table, pinball machine or
video game, and where such a fee is collected by an operator and the game
activated by the operator.
PINBALL MACHINE: Any pinball or pinball machine, or marble machine, or any
other similar type of game or machine or table in which any ball, sphere,
missile, arm, crane, appliance, rod or plunger is struck, released, impelled,
controlled, or manipulated directly or indirectly for the purpose of amusement
or skill and in which a test of skill is involved, and for the playing of which
a fee is charged.
POOL TABLE: Any table or device designed and/or utilized to play pool or
billiards including, but not limited to, six (6) pocket billiard tables, pocket
billiards, billiards or bumper pool.
VIDEO GAME: Includes any electrical or mechanical device projecting targets,
obstacles or games upon a TV video screen and in which a player may manipulate
electronic responses to the obstacles, targets or games projected upon the
video screen. (Ord. 1040, 4-19-1982, eff. 6-1-1982)
3-3-2: LICENSE REQUIRED:
It shall be required that all coin operated amusement devices be licensed each
year. (Ord. 1040, 4-19-1982, eff. 6-1-1982)
3-3-3: APPLICATION FOR LICENSE; INVESTIGATION AND APPROVAL:
   A.   Submittal Of Application; Contents: Applications for a license to
operate coin operated amusement devices shall be made to the city clerk, in
writing, on a form to be furnished by the city clerk to the applicant. The
application must state the full name of the operator, the operator's legal
business address, and the operator's business telephone number, and must fully
state and describe the nature and type of the coin operated amusement devices
to be operated.
   B.   Investigation Of Applicant: Upon the application being prepared and
executed by the applicant, the same shall be submitted to the mayor for
approval. The mayor may withhold action on the application for ten (10) days
for investigation of the application file before taking action thereon. (Ord.
1040, 4-19-1982, eff. 6-1-1982)
3-3-4: LICENSE FEES:
For each coin operated amusement device or pool table, pinball machine or video
game operated for profit within the city, including any such device where a
player must pay some monetary consideration to play such device, an annual
license fee shall be imposed as follows:
   A.   Pool Tables: All pool tables shall be licensed for the sum of twenty
five dollars ($25.00) per table, per year.
   B.   Pinball Machines: All pinball machines shall be licensed for the sum of
twenty five dollars ($25.00) per year.
   C.   Video Games: All video game machines shall be licensed for the sum of
twenty five dollars ($25.00) per year.
   D.   Other Table Games: All table games not heretofore mentioned in this
section shall be licensed for the sum of twenty five dollars ($25.00) per year,
per table game. (Ord. 1098, 7-15-1985, eff. 6-1-1986)
3-3-5: TERM OF LICENSE; DISPOSITION OF FEES:
A license issued under this chapter shall be valid for one year. The twelve
(12) month period shall be from June 1 of each year to May 31 of the succeeding
year. The annual license fee shall be payable in advance by the applicant for a
license at the time the application for a license is submitted to the city
clerk as hereinafter provided. In the event the license is denied, the license
fee shall be returned to the applicant. The fees shall be deposited with the
city treasurer, who shall deposit such fees in the city general fund. (Ord.
1040, 4-19-1982, eff. 6-1-1982; amd. 2006 Code)
3-3-6: GAMBLING:
No person is permitted to gamble or wage any bets for a money or other valuable
consideration on the outcome of any game played or any pool table, pinball
machine or video game licensed by this chapter. This prohibition, however,
shall not apply to any game or gaming event for which a license or permit has
been issued by the Illinois department of revenue pursuant to the pull tabs and
jar games act, 230 Illinois Compiled Statutes 20/1 et seq., the bingo license
and tax act, 230 Illinois Compiled Statutes 25/1 et seq., the Illinois video
gaming act, 230 Illinois Compiled Statutes 40/1 et seq., or the charitable
games act, 230 Illinois Compiled Statutes 30/1 et seq., so long as such game or
gaming event is conducted in compliance with all requirements of said acts and
all rules and regulations of the Illinois department of revenue. Any person
gambling on the outcome of a game played on a pool table, pinball machine or
video game except as permitted herein shall be guilty of a petty offense and
fined not in excess of thirty five dollars ($35.00), plus court costs. (Ord.
1457, 6-18-2012)
3-3-7: VIOLATION; PENALTY:
Any owner or operator violating any section of this chapter shall be guilty of
a petty offense and shall be fined as provided in section
1-4-1 of this code, plus court costs. (Ord. 1040, 4-19-1982, eff. 6-1-1982;
amd. 2006 Code)
CHAPTER 4
PEDDLERS
SECTION:
3-4-1: Definitions
3-4-2: License Required
3-4-3: Application For License
3-4-4: License Fees
3-4-5: Issuance Of License
3-4-6: Possession And Display Of License
3-4-7: Restrictions On License
3-4-8: Revocation Or Suspension Of License
3-4-9: Penalty
3-4-1: DEFINITIONS:
As used in this chapter, the following words and terms shall have the meanings
ascribed to them in this section:
MOTOR VEHICLE: Any vehicle used for the displaying, storing or transporting of
articles offered for sale by a vendor which is required to be licensed and
registered with the secretary of state of Illinois. The term is to include
trailers, trucks and automobiles.
PEDDLER: A. Every person who shall sell or offer for sale, barter or exchange,
at retail, any goods, wares or merchandise from a stationary stand or vehicle
or by traveling from place to place in, along and upon the streets, avenues,
alleys or public thoroughfares of the city, or who shall sell and deliver from
any vehicle goods, wares or merchandise by going from place to place in the
city, whether to regular customers or not.
   B.   The term "peddler" shall also mean every person who moves from house to
house or from place to place in the city selling or taking orders for goods,
wares, subscriptions or merchandise for future delivery.
   C.   The term "peddler" shall not include the following two (2) groups of
persons:
1. Farmers, fruit growers and gardeners who sell the produce of their farm,
orchard, or vineyard from a stand.
2. Sellers or deliverers of newspapers.
STAND: Any table, showcase, bench, rack, pushcart, wagon or any other wheeled
vehicle or device which may be moved without the assistance of a motor and
which is not required to be licensed and registered with the secretary of state
of Illinois. (Ord. 1050, 11-1-1982, eff. 1-1-1983)
3-4-2: LICENSE REQUIRED:
No person may engage in the business of a peddler without first obtaining a
license to do so. Any civic, patriotic, fraternal, educational, religious or
benevolent organization may obtain one license for the entire group to be held
and displayed by the president or leader of said organization. (Ord. 1050, 11-
1-1982, eff. 1-1-1983)
3-4-3: APPLICATION FOR LICENSE:
An application for a peddler's license shall be made in writing to the city
clerk who shall require the following:
   A.   The name of the individual applying for the license;
   B.   The residence, telephone number and driver's license number of the
applicant;
   C.   The address of the principal place of business of the applicant and his
telephone number;
   D.   If the applicant is employed by another person or entity, the name of
the employer, his address and telephone number;
   E.   The type of goods, wares or merchandise to be sold or offered for sale;
   F.   The location where the applicant plans to sell his goods, wares or
merchandise;
   G.   Whether the applicant has been convicted of a criminal offense or
ordinance violation (other than traffic or parking offenses) in any
jurisdiction and, if so, a list of such convictions with date and prosecuting
jurisdiction; and
   H.   Current state of Illinois sales tax certificate. (Ord. 1050, 11-1-1982,
eff. 1-1-1983)
3-4-4: LICENSE FEES:
   A.   Fees Enumerated: The applicant shall pay the following fees to the city
clerk prior to filing an application. All fees shall be paid into the city's
general fund. Should the application be denied, the license fee shall be
refunded to the applicant: (Ord. 1050, 11-1-1982, eff. 1-1-1983; amd. 2006
Code)
      1.   Annual Fee: Fifty dollars ($50.00) per calendar year or part
thereof. If the applicant is associated with a company or organization whose
member has previously paid a yearly fee of fifty dollars ($50.00), then this
applicant's fee will be twenty dollars ($20.00) for a calendar year or part
thereof.
      2.   Weekly Fee: Ten dollars ($10.00) for a seven (7) day license
beginning on the day of issuance and running for seven (7) consecutive days. If
the applicant is associated with a company or organization whose member has
previously paid a seven (7) day fee of ten dollars ($10.00), then this
applicant's fee will be four dollars ($4.00) for seven (7) days.
   B.   Exemptions From Fees: No fee shall be required when the applicant is a
group or person:
      1.   Who, without receiving any compensation for his services, solicits
contributions or sells goods, wares or merchandise for civic, patriotic,
fraternal, educational, religious or benevolent organizations;
      2.   Who sells goods, wares or merchandise on city owned public grounds
as part of an event which has been approved by the city clerk; and
      3.   Who sells at events which are sponsored by civic, patriotic,
fraternal, educational, religious or benevolent organizations goods, wares or
merchandise which they have made themselves such as handicrafts and home sewn
items. (Ord. 1050, 11-1-1982, eff. 1-1-1983)
3-4-5: ISSUANCE OF LICENSE:
The city clerk shall issue the license, running from the date of issuance until
December 31 of the calendar year, unless he shall find:
   A.   That the applicant has been convicted within the last five (5) years of
any offense relating to theft, burglary, or fraud; or
   B.   That the applicant or his employer has had a license issued pursuant to
this chapter revoked for cause. (Ord. 1050, 11-1-1982, eff. 1-1-1983)
3-4-6: POSSESSION AND DISPLAY OF LICENSE:
All licensees shall have in their possession at all times while engaging in
business as a peddler the license issued to them by the city and shall show it
to any person who requests to see it. Any civic, patriotic, fraternal,
educational, religious or benevolent organization may obtain one license for
the entire group to be held and displayed by the president or leader of said
organization. (Ord. 1050, 11-1-1982, eff. 1-1-1983)
3-4-7: RESTRICTIONS ON LICENSE:
   A.   Hours: No one shall engage in the business of a peddler between the
hours of ten o'clock (10:00) P.M. and ten o'clock (10:00) A.M.
   B.   Location:
      1.   No peddler shall park or stand within two hundred feet (200') of a
playground or school during the time that organized recreational activities are
in progress.
      2.   No peddler shall sell or offer for sale goods, wares or merchandise
other than at the location approved by the city.
   C.   Sales From Vehicles: Whenever a peddler shall make sales from a
vehicle, the vehicle shall be stopped at the right hand curb of the street or
at the extreme right hand edge of the pavement. No sales shall be made from any
vehicle except from the curb side thereof.
   D.   Peddling At Residences:
      1.   No person shall engage in the business of peddling at any residence
at which there is displayed upon or near the main entrance door a weatherproof
card, approximately three inches by four inches (3" x 4"), which states one of
the following:
   NO SOLICITORS INVITED
   or
   NO PEDDLERS INVITED
or words to the same effect. Lettering on such signs shall be at least one-
third inch (1/3") in height.
      2.   No peddler shall remain at any residence after being asked by an
occupant to leave.
   E.   Unattended Stands: No peddler shall leave any stand unattended.
   F.   Stands Overnight On Public Ways: No peddler shall store, park or leave
any stand overnight on any street, sidewalk or public right of way.
   G.   Parking Vehicles: No peddler shall park any motor vehicle other than in
a lawful parking place in conformance with city and state parking regulations.
   H.   Garbage And Refuse:
      1.   All peddlers selling food and beverages for immediate consumption
shall have available for public use their own litter receptacle which is
available for use by their patrons.
      2.   No peddler shall leave his location without first picking up,
removing and disposing of all trash or refuse from the sales made by him.
   I.   Soliciting Persons In Vehicles: No peddler shall solicit or conduct
business with persons in motor vehicles.
   J.   Items To Be Sold: No peddler shall sell anything other than that which
he stated in his license application. (Ord. 1050, 11-1-1982, eff. 1-1-1983)
3-4-8: REVOCATION OR SUSPENSION OF LICENSE:
   A.   Conditions For Revocation Or Suspension: Any peddler's license may be
revoked, or suspended for a period not to exceed one year, by the city clerk,
if the city council shall find after a hearing:
      1.   That the licensee has violated any of the provisions of this
chapter, the laws of the state, or the ordinances of the city while engaged in
the business as a peddler, other than traffic or parking offenses.
      2.   That the licensee has knowingly furnished false or misleading
information or withheld relevant information on any application for a peddler's
license or an investigation into any such license.
   B.   Hearing: Prior to holding a hearing concerning the question of whether
a license issued pursuant to this chapter shall be revoked or suspended, the
city clerk shall give at least ten (10) days' written notice to the licensee
setting forth the alleged violations specifically. The licensee may present
evidence at such hearing and cross examine witnesses. (Ord. 1050, 11-1-1982,
eff. 1-1-1983)
3-4-9: PENALTY:
Any person who fails to obtain a license in violation of this chapter shall,
upon conviction thereof, be subject to a fine as provided in section
1-4-1 of this code. (Ord. 1050, 11-1-1982, eff. 1-1-1983; amd. 2006 Code)
CHAPTER 5
OIL AND GAS OPERATIONS
SECTION:
3-5-1: Permit Required
3-5-2: Application For Permit; Fee
3-5-3: Consideration Of Application; Hearing
3-5-4: Issuance Of Permit
3-5-5: Conditions Of Permit
3-5-6: Term Of Permit
3-5-7: Revocation Of Permit
3-5-8: Nuisance Declared
3-5-9: Violations; Penalty
3-5-1: PERMIT REQUIRED:
No oil or gas well or other facility used directly in the production of oil or
gas shall be established, drilled, operated or commenced in the city until the
operator or other responsible person in charge shall have obtained a permit
issued in compliance with this chapter. (Ord. 762, 9-6-1960)
3-5-2: APPLICATION FOR PERMIT; FEE:
Anyone desiring a permit under this chapter shall submit an application under
oath stating the exact location of the proposed well location or installation,
the distance to any structures on adjacent premises and the type of structures
involved, the exact nature of the operation for which permit is requested,
including pits, tanks, etc., the area unitized, or intended to be unitized and
which will be served by the well, the amount of the area under lease to the
applicant, and the term of the lease, and the name and address of the
applicant, operator or other persons who will be responsible for the operation.
A one hundred dollar ($100.00) fee will be paid the city clerk at the time of
the filing of the application. (Ord. 762, 9-6-1960)
3-5-3: CONSIDERATION OF APPLICATION; HEARING:
The city council shall consider the information contained in the application
and such other information relating to the health, safety and welfare of the
city, including, but not by way of limitation, fire hazard, safety of citizens,
especially children, traffic hazard, appearance of community, nuisance to
nearby inhabitants, amount of unleased property in unitized area, size of
unitized area, location and effect on utility facilities, specific plan of
operator for location of rig, pits, tanks, and other facilities, effect on
streets, and other relevant information. The council may, at its discretion,
require answers under oath to questions in this regard to be attached to the
application for permit or may hold a hearing, or delegate the holding of a
hearing, as it sees fit. Statements by the applicant or his representative at
such a hearing shall be deemed a part of the application. (Ord. 762, 9-6-1960)
3-5-4: ISSUANCE OF PERMIT:
If the city council is of the opinion that the issuance of a permit is not
detrimental to the health, safety and welfare of the city, it may issue a
permit to the applicant. The vote to issue a permit shall be as for any
resolution. No more than one permit per pool shall be issued for each block.
The permit shall be issued by the city clerk. (Ord. 762, 9-6-1960)
3-5-5: CONDITIONS OF PERMIT:
The city council shall have the power to condition the issuance of a permit in
such a way as to require certain standards to be met; types of equipment to be
used; locations to be conformed to; time schedules for operation to be adhered
to; bond to be posted for individual or corporate damage; health, welfare and
safety measures to be complied with; damages or other monies to be paid to the
city in the event property will be damaged or additional city expense shall be
incurred; or other measures deemed reasonably necessary for the health, safety
or welfare of the city. Any applicant who commences operation under a permit
issued will be conclusively deemed to have accepted the conditions of the
permit. (Ord. 762, 9-6-1960)
3-5-6: TERM OF PERMIT:
The permit shall be issued for such period as the council shall direct, but
shall not exceed the term of the shortest lease in the unitized area. If no
term is stated, it shall be for ninety (90) days and as long thereafter as oil
or gas is produced. (Ord. 762, 9-6-1960)
3-5-7: REVOCATION OF PERMIT:
The city council may, by resolution, revoke any permit issued when the
applicant has made false material statements in his application and additional
information requested. The permit shall be valid up to the date of revocation.
(Ord. 762, 9-6-1960; amd. 2006 Code)
3-5-8: NUISANCE DECLARED:
Any oil or gas well or other facility described herein operated without a valid
permit under this chapter or in a manner materially varying from the
description in the application and other information submitted or the
conditions of the permit is declared a public nuisance. (Ord. 762, 9-6-1960)
3-5-9: VIOLATIONS; PENALTY:
   A.   False Statements Deemed Perjury: Any applicant who makes a false
statement in his application for a permit, to include all answers subsequently
given pursuant thereto, shall be guilty of perjury as provided by the laws of
the state. (Ord. 762, 9-6-1960)
   B.   Penalty: Any operator, driller, owner of a leasehold, or portion
thereof, or person actively engaged in operations defined herein who operates
any installation described in this chapter without a permit shall be, upon
conviction, fined as provided in section
1-4-1 of this code for each violation. Every day upon which such violation
shall occur or upon which such violation shall continue shall constitute a
separate offense. (Ord. 762, 9-6-1960; amd. 2006 Code)
CHAPTER 6
RAFFLES
SECTION:
3-6-1: Definitions
3-6-2: License
3-6-3: Application
3-6-4: Validity Of License
3-6-5: Ineligibility For License
3-6-6: Not For Profit Organizations
3-6-7: Limitations
3-6-8: Fees
3-6-9: Approval
3-6-10: Conduct Of Raffles
3-6-11: Records
3-6-12: Manager's Bond
3-6-13: Suspension/Revocation
3-6-14: Punishment
3-6-1: DEFINITIONS:
BUSINESS: A voluntary organization composed of individuals and businesses who
have joined together to advance the commercial, financial, industrial and civil
interests of a community.
CHARITABLE: An organization or institution organized and operated to benefit an
indefinite number of the public. The service rendered to those eligible for
benefits must also confer some benefit on the public.
EDUCATIONAL: An organization or institution organized and operated to provide
systematic instruction in useful branches of learning by methods common to
schools and institutions of learning which compare favorably in their scope and
intensity with the course of study presented in tax-supported schools.
FRATERNAL: An organization of persons having a common interest, the primary
interest of which is to both promote the welfare of its members and to provide
assistance to the general public in such a way as to lessen the burdens of
government by caring for those that otherwise would be cared for by the
government.
LABOR: An organization composed of workers organized with the objective of
betterment of the conditions of a higher degree of efficiency in their
respective occupations.
NET PROCEEDS: The gross receipts from the conduct of raffles, less reasonable
sums expended for prizes, license fees, and other reasonable operating expenses
incurred as a result of operating a raffle.
NON-PROFIT: An organization or institution organized and conducted on a not-
for-profit basis with no personal profit inuring to anyone as a result of the
operation.
RAFFLE: A form of lottery, as defined in section 28-2(b) of the "Criminal Code
of 1961", conducted by an organization licensed under this chapter, in which:
   A.   The player pays or agrees to pay something of value for a chance,
represented and differentiated by a number or by a combination of numbers or by
some other medium, one (1) or more of which chances is to be designated the
winning chance;
   B.   The winning chance is to be determined through a drawing or by some
other method based on an element of chance by an act or set of acts on the part
of persons conducting or connected with the lottery, except that the winning
chance shall not be determined by the outcome of a publicly exhibited sporting
contest.
RELIGIOUS: Any church, congregation, society, or organization founded for the
purposes of religious worship.
VETERANS: An organization or association comprised of members of whom
substantially all are individuals who are veterans of military service, the
primary purpose of which is to promote the welfare of its members and to
provide assistance to the general public in such a way as to confer a public
benefit. (Ord. 1505, 7-5-2016)
3-6-2: LICENSE:
   A.   License Required: No person, firm, corporation or other entity shall
conduct raffles or chances without having first obtained a license therefor
pursuant to this chapter and the "Raffles Act". (Ord. 1505, 7-5-2016)
3-6-3: APPLICATION:
   A.   Applications shall be made in writing through the City Clerk's Office
at least thirty (30) days prior to the first day intended for sale of the
raffle chances. The application shall be on a form furnished by the City Clerk.
   B.   Applications for licenses under this chapter must contain the following
information:
      1.   Name of applicant.
      2.   Address.
      3.   Purpose of raffle.
      4.   Area within the City where the raffle is to be conducted.
      5.   Time period during which chances will be sold or issued.
      6.   Sworn statement attesting to not-for-profit character of the
prospective license organization, signed by the presiding officer and secretary
of the organization.
      7.   Date, time and location at which winning chances will be determined.
      8.   The aggregate retail value of all prizes or merchandise to be
awarded by a single raffle.
      9.   The maximum retail value of each prize or each specific type of
prize to be awarded by a license in a single raffle.
      10.   The maximum to be charged for each raffle chance and the number of
chances to be issued for each raffle.
      11.   The name(s) and address(es) of the operator of the raffle if not an
officer or member of the applicant organization. (Ord. 1505, 7-5-2016)
3-6-4: VALIDITY OF LICENSE:
Each such license shall be valid for one (1) raffle or for a specified number
of raffles during a specified period not to exceed one (1) year, and may be
suspended or revoked by the Corporate Authorities in the event of violation of
the terms of this chapter or of any applicable State law. (Ord. 1505, 7-5-2016)
3-6-5: INELIGIBILITY FOR LICENSE:
   A.   The following are ineligible for any license under this chapter:
      1.   Any person who has been convicted of a felony;
      2.   Any person who is or has been a professional gambler or gambling
promoter;
      3.   Any person who is not of good moral character;
      4.   Any firm or corporation in which a person defined in subsection A1,
A2, or A3 of this section has a proprietary, equitable or credit interest, or
in which such a person is active or employed;
      5.   Any organization in which a person defined in subsection A1, A2, or
A3 of this section is an officer, director or employee, whether compensated or
not;
      6.   Any organization in which a person defined in subsection A1, A2, or
A3 of this section is to participate in the management or operation of a raffle
as defined in the "Raffles Act". (Ord. 1505, 7-5-2016)
3-6-6: NOT FOR PROFIT ORGANIZATIONS:
Licenses shall be issued only to bona fide non-profit religious, charitable,
labor, business, fraternal, educational or veterans' organizations as defined
in section
3-6-1 of this chapter which operate without profit to their members and which
have been in existence continuously for a period of five (5) years immediately
before making application for a license and which have had during that entire
five (5) year period a bona fide membership engaged in carrying out their
objectives, or to a non-profit fund raising organization that the licensing
authority determines is organized for the sole purpose of providing financial
assistance to an identified individual or group of individuals suffering
extreme financial hardships as the result of an illness, disability, accident
or disaster. (Ord. 1505, 7-5-2016)
3-6-7: LIMITATIONS:
   A.   The aggregate retail value of all prizes or merchandise awarded by a
licensee in a single raffle under this chapter and in accordance with
applicable State law is limited to two hundred fifty thousand dollars
($250,000.00).
   B.   The maximum retail value of each prize awarded by a licensee in a
single raffle is limited to two hundred thousand dollars ($200,000.00).
   C.   The maximum price which may be charged for each raffle chance issued or
sold is limited to one hundred dollars ($100.00).
   D.   The maximum number of days during which raffle chances may be issued or
sold for any one (1) raffle shall be one (1) year.
   E.   Licenses issued shall be valid for one (1) raffle or for a specified
number of raffles to be conducted during a specified period not to exceed one
(1) year and may be suspended or revoked for any violation of the "Raffles Act"
or this chapter. (Ord. 1505, 7-5-2016)
3-6-8: FEES:
The fee for such a license to conduct a raffle shall be five dollars ($5.00).
(Ord. 1505, 7-5-2016)
3-6-9: APPROVAL:
The City of Carmi shall, within thirty (30) days, evaluate and either approve
or disapprove of said application. The City's approval of an application for a
license shall constitute the license for the conduct of the raffle applied for
by the applicant. (Ord. 1505, 7-5-2016)
3-6-10: CONDUCT OF RAFFLES:
The conducting of raffles is subject to the following restrictions:
   A.   Proceeds: The entire net proceeds of any raffle must be exclusively
devoted to the lawful purpose of the organization permitted to conduct that
game.
   B.   Participation In Management: No person except a bona fide member of the
sponsoring organization may participate in the management or operation of the
raffle.
   C.   Remuneration: No person may receive any remuneration or profit for
participating in the management or operation of the raffle.
   D.   Premises: A licensee may rent a premises on which to determine the
winning chance or chances in a raffle only from an organization which is also
licensed under this chapter.
   E.   Locations: Raffle chances may be sold or issued only within the area
specified on the license and winning chances may be determined only at those
locations specified on the license.
   F.   Age Of Participants: No person under the age of eighteen (18) years may
participate in the conducting of raffles or chances. A person under the age of
eighteen (18) years may be within the area where winning chances are being
determined only when accompanied by his/her parent or guardian.
   G.   Location For Determining Winning Chance(s): The location of the
premises on which to determine the winning chance or chances in a raffle shall
be restricted to a business district, commercial district or where a special
use permit has been granted for a school, church, government or similar
institution. (Ord. 1505, 7-5-2016)
3-6-11: RECORDS:
   A.   Each organization licensed to conduct raffles and chances shall keep
such records and shall also keep records of its gross receipts, expenses and
net proceeds for each single gathering or occasion at which chances are
determined.
   B.   Gross receipts from the operation of raffles programs shall be
segregated from other revenues of the organization, including bingo gross
receipts, if bingo games are also conducted by the same nonprofit organization
pursuant to license therefor issued by the Department of Revenue of the State
of Illinois, and shall be placed in a separate account. Each organization shall
have separate records of its raffles. The person who accounts for gross
receipts, expenses and net proceeds from the operation of raffles shall not be
the same person who accounts for other revenues of the organization.
   C.   Each organization licensed to conduct raffles shall report promptly
after the conclusion of each raffle to its membership, and to the City of
Carmi, its gross receipts, expenses and net proceeds from raffles, and the
distribution of net proceeds itemized as required in this section.
   D.   Records required by this section shall be preserved three (3) years,
and organizations shall make available their records relating to operation of
raffles for public inspection at reasonable times and places. (Ord. 1505, 7-5-
2016)
3-6-12: MANAGER'S BOND:
All operations of and conduct of raffles shall be under the supervision of a
single raffles manager designated by the organization. The manager or operator
of the raffle must be a bona fide member of the organization holding the
license for such a raffle and may not receive any remuneration or profit for
participating in the management or operation of the raffle. The manager shall
give a fidelity bond in the sum of the total value of the prizes to be awarded
in the raffle conditioned upon his/her honesty in the performance of his/her
duties. Terms of the bond shall provide that notice shall be given in writing
to the City not less than thirty (30) days prior to its cancellation. The City
may waive this bond requirement by including a waiver provision in the license
issued to an organization under this chapter, provided that a license
containing such waiver provision shall be granted only by unanimous vote of the
members of the City Council. (Ord. 1505, 7-5-2016)
3-6-13: SUSPENSION/REVOCATION:
Any license granted under this chapter may be suspended or revoked by the City
at any time it appears that the proposed or actual operation of the raffle will
be or is such as to constitute a public nuisance or to endanger the public
peace, health, safety or welfare. Any license granted under this chapter may be
suspended or revoked in whole or in part at any time that the raffle is
conducted contrary to the license or to any State or City law, or when such
raffle or portion thereof is conducted so as to constitute a public nuisance or
to disturb the peace, health, safety or welfare. Suspension or revocation shall
become effective immediately. It shall be a violation for any person to
operate, engage or participate in, except as a patron, any raffle which license
has been suspended or revoked. (Ord. 1505, 7-5-2016)
3-6-14: PUNISHMENT:
Any raffle permit issued under this chapter shall be revoked or suspended if
the permit holder violates any terms of the license or any other provisions of
this chapter. Any violation of this chapter shall be subject to a fine up to
seven hundred fifty dollars ($750.00). Each day that a violation hereof exists
shall be considered a separate offense. Each raffle held in violation hereof
shall be considered a separate offense. (Ord. 1505, 7-5-2016)
CHAPTER 7
TOBACCO PRODUCT AND CANNABIS SALES
SECTION:
3-7-1: Tobacco, Tobacco Products, Electronic Cigarettes And Alternative
Nicotine Products
3-7-2: Cannabis
3-7-3: Penalties
3-7-1: TOBACCO, TOBACCO PRODUCTS, ELECTRONIC CIGARETTES AND ALTERNATIVE
NICOTINE PRODUCTS:
   (A)   No person under twenty-one (21) years of age shall buy any tobacco,
tobacco product, electronic cigarettes, or alternative nicotine products in the
City of Carmi White County, Illinois.
   (B)   No person, regardless of age, shall sell, buy for, distribute samples
of or furnish any tobacco, tobacco products, electronic cigarettes, or
alternative nicotine products to any minor under twenty-one (21) years of age.
   (C)   No person under sixteen (16) years of age may sell any tobacco
product, electronic cigarette, or alternative nicotine product at a retail
establishment authorized in selling tobacco products, electronic cigarettes, or
alternative nicotine products. This subsection does not apply to a sales clerk
in a family-owned business which can prove that the sales clerk is in fact a
son or daughter of the owner.
   (D)   No minor under twenty-one (21) years of age in the furtherance or
facilitation of obtaining any tobacco product, electronic cigarette, or
alternative nicotine product shall display or use a false or forged
identification card or transfer, alter, or deface an identification card.
   (E)   No minor under twenty-one (21) years of age shall possess any cigar,
cigarette, smokeless tobacco, tobacco in any form, electronic cigarette or
alternative nicotine product in any of its forms.
   (F)   Definitions: As used in this chapter:
 
                               A product or device not consisting of or
                               containing tobacco that provides for the
ALTERNATIVE NICOTINE PRODUCTS: ingestion into the body of nicotine, whether by
                               chewing, smoking, absorbing, dissolving,
                               inhaling, snorting, sniffing, or by any other
                               means.
                               E-cigarettes, vapes, vape or hookah pens, vape
ELECTRONIC CIGARETTE:          pens, e-pipes, other vaping products, and any
                               battery-powered devices that allow users to
                               inhale, or vape, aerosolized liquid (e-juice).
SMOKELESS TOBACCO:             Any tobacco products that are suitable for
                               dipping or chewing.
                               Any cigar, cigarette, smokeless tobacco, or
TOBACCO PRODUCT:               tobacco content in any of its forms. (Ord. 1562,
                               8-4-2020)
 
3-7-2: CANNABIS:
   (A)   No persons under twenty-one (21) years of age shall purchase, possess,
use, process, transport, grow, or consume cannabis except where authorized by
the Compassionate Use of Medical Cannabis Program Act.
   (B)   Definitions: As used in this chapter:
 
          Includes marijuana, hashish and other substances which are identified
          as including any parts of the plant Cannabis Sativa, whether growing
          or not; the seeds thereof, the resin extracted from any part of such
          plant; and any compound, manufacture, salt, derivative, mixture, or
CANNABIS: preparation of such plant, its seeds, or resin, including
          tetrahydrocannabinol (THC) and all other cannabinol derivatives,
          including its naturally occurring or synthetically produced
          ingredients, whether produced directly or indirectly by extraction,
          or independently by means of chemical synthesis or by a combination
          of extraction and chemical synthesis. (Ord. 1562, 8-4-2020)
 
3-7-3: PENALTIES:
   (A)   Any person violating any provisions of this chapter shall be fined one
hundred fifty dollars ($150.00) for the first offense.
   (B)   Any person violating any provisions of this chapter shall be fined not
less than one hundred fifty dollars ($150.00) nor more than seven hundred fifty
dollars ($750.00) for a second or subsequent offense. (Ord. 1562, 8-4-2020)
TITLE 4
PUBLIC HEALTH AND SAFETY
CHAPTER 1
FIRE DEPARTMENT
SECTION:
4-1-1: Department Created; Members
4-1-2: Officers
4-1-3: Compensation
4-1-4: Powers And Duties Of Fire Chief And Assistants
4-1-5: Duties Of Secretary
4-1-6: Bond And Duties Of Treasurer; Department Funds
4-1-7: Duties Of Department Members
4-1-8: Obedience And Aid During Fires
4-1-9: Traffic Regulations During Fires
4-1-10: Fire Department Equipment
4-1-11: Fire Service For Non-Residents
4-1-12: Enforcement
4-1-1: DEPARTMENT CREATED; MEMBERS:
There is hereby created and established a Fire Department consisting of a Fire
Chief, Assistant Fire Chief, two Captains, a Secretary/Treasurer, and such
members of said Fire Department as may from time to time be determined and
appointed by the Mayor and City Council. (Ord. 1616, 2-6-2024)
4-1-2: OFFICERS:
   A.   Fire Chief: The fire chief of the city fire department shall hereafter
be appointed and employed by the mayor with the consent of the city council.
   B.   Other Officers: The fire department shall meet the third Wednesday in
June and at this meeting shall elect one assistant fire chief, from their
members, and if any vacancies in membership occur, said vacancies shall be
filled by voting from names submitted by the fire chief. These officers and
members shall be approved by the mayor and city council. After approval and
qualifying, these officers shall take office the first Wednesday after the
first Monday in July. Captains shall be appointed by the Fire Chief upon taking
command, and Captains shall serve a term of two years. (Ord. 997, 5-19-1980;
amd. ; 2006 Code; Ord. 1616, 2-6-2024)
4-1-3: COMPENSATION:
   A.   Salaried Positions: The salary of the fire chief shall be fifteen
hundred dollars ($1500.00) per month; the salary of the assistant fire chief
shall be four hundred dollars ($400.00) per month; the salary of the secretary/
treasurer of the fire department shall be twenty-three hundred dollars
($2300.00) per month; any captain shall receive two hundred fifty dollars
($250.00) each month all payable by the city treasurer from the city general
fund. Each salaried member, upon willfully and diligently carrying out the
duties in extinguishing a fire or performing other duties warranted by call
sheet, shall be paid the sum of sixty dollars ($60.00) per call sheet by the
City of Carmi general funds.
   B.   Firefighters: Payment to volunteers shall be on a Per Call Basis and
shall cover Expenses, Reasonable Benefits, and a Nominal Fee in accordance with
the Department of Labor’s Fair Labor Standards Act.
      1.   Probationary members shall receive thirty-five dollars ($35.00) per
fire call and for all other duties warranted by call sheet.
      2.   Full members shall receive fifty dollars ($50.00) per fire call and
for all other duties warranted by call sheet. Full members shall also receive
for themselves and their household family members access to the Tri-State
Community Clinic, paid for by the City of Carmi.
   C.   Multiple Department Response: Any fire fighter who is a member of the
Carmi Fire Department, along with another department, will be paid by the first
department for which they first respond.
   D.   City of Carmi Employees: Article XIX Section 19.6 Volunteer Fireman of
the City of Carmi’s AFSCME Union Contract clearly states; “Any City of Carmi
employee who is a member of the City of Carmi volunteer fire department shall
be paid his/her normal rate of pay if he/she is called to respond to a fire
call while on duty with the City. No employee will be eligible for overtime
payment if the call extends beyond the employee’s normal quitting time or the
employee is called to respond outside of his/her normal time to work.”
   E.   Changes to Compensation:
      1.   Any proposed changes by the City of Carmi to the compensation of the
Carmi Fire Department must gain prior approval by vote of the full members of
the Carmi Fire Department and upon adoption be updated within the By-Laws of
the Carmi Volunteer Fire Company.
      2.   Any proposed changes by the Carmi Fire Department to the
compensation of the Carmi Fire Department must gain prior approval by vote of
the Carmi City Council and upon adoption be updated within the By-Laws of the
Carmi Volunteer Fire Company. (Ord. 711, 5-2-1955; amd. 2006 Code; Ord. 1616,
2-6-2024)
4-1-4: POWERS AND DUTIES OF FIRE CHIEF AND ASSISTANTS:
   A.   Appoint Department Members: The fire chief shall, upon taking office,
appoint such personnel and prescribe such duties as may be necessary and proper
in the organization and effective operation of the fire department during that
year.
   B.   Control And Supervision of Department: The fire chief shall have the
control and supervision, subject to the order and direction of the city
council, of the fire department and all fire apparatus and equipment belonging
to the city.
   C.   Command At Fires: In case of fire, the fire chief and his assistants,
in their order of rank, shall take command at such fire, and the officer
highest in rank shall take command of the fire department and direct the
management thereof for the suppression of the fire in the best manner possible,
and when it may be necessary for protection of other property to prevent the
spread of the conflagration, the officer in command may cause buildings to be
removed, torn down, or destroyed in the best manner possible.
   D.   Drills: It shall also be the duty of the fire chief to call drill
meetings as he sees fit.
   E.   Further Details and Duties: A detailed description of job duties shall
be kept up to date in the department’s by-laws and/or standard operating
guidelines. (Ord. 1616, 2-6-2024)
4-1-5: DUTIES OF SECRETARY:
The secretary shall keep a record of all meetings of the department and the
attendance of the members, a record of all fires and the attendance of the
members at such fires, and, during the last week of June of each year, file
with the city clerk, a full report of such record of attendance and fires which
said report shall be made under oath. He shall also keep such other records,
make such reports, and keep and furnish such statistics as may be required by
him by law. (Ord. 1616, 2-6-2024)
4-1-6: BOND AND DUTIES OF TREASURER; DEPARTMENT FUNDS:
   A.   Bond: The treasurer, before taking office, shall execute and file with
the city clerk, a sufficient bond to the city, to be approved by the mayor and
city council, conditioned for the faithful performance of his duties under this
chapter.
   B.   Department Funds:
      1.   Money collected on behalf of the firefighters, such as dues,
donations and fundraising, shall be deposited into the Carmi Fireman’s
Association account.
      2.   Money collected in regard to fire department response shall be
deposited into the City of Carmi’s General Fund as required by the Illinois
Municipal Code.
      3.   Money collected in accordance with the Foreign Fire Insurance
License Fee shall be deposited into the Foreign Fire Board account as required.
   C.   Reports Required: The treasurer shall make monthly reports to the fire
department of the condition of the funds in his hands and shall, on the first
Tuesday of December in each year, make a sworn report and statement to the
mayor and city council of al! monies received and disbursed by him as such
treasurer and the balance of monies in his hands.
   D.   Books, Records and Accounts:
      1.   The books, records and accounts of the treasurer shall be faithfully
kept and shall, at ail times, be open to inspection and audit of the mayor and
city council.
      2.   The treasurer shall, at the expiration of his term of office,
surrender, pay and deliver to his successor in office, all books, records,
accounts and monies in his hands as treasurer. (2006 Code; amd. Ord. 1616, 2-6-
2024)
4-1-7: DUTIES OF DEPARTMENT MEMBERS:
It shall be the function and duties of the fire department and every member
thereof to extinguish accidental or ^destructive fires, to prevent the
occurrence or spread of fires, and to enforce all ordinances relating to the
occurrence or spread of such fires. (Ord. 1616, 2-6-2024)
4-1-8: OBEDIENCE AND AID DURING FIRES:
   A.   Obedience To Command During Fires: No firefighter in attendance at a
fire shall neglect or refuse to obey the orders of the officer in command at
such fires.
   B.   Aid During Fires:
      1.   Every person above the age of twenty-one who shall be present at a
fire shall be subject to the orders of the officer in command at such fire and
shall render all the assistance in his power and in such manner as he may be
directed in the extinguishing of the fire, and in the removal of and protection
of property, he shall obey such orders. In refusing to do so, said person
shall, upon conviction, be fined as provided in section
1-4-1  of this code, provided no person shall be bound to obey any such
officer, unless such officer’s official character shall be known to such
person.
      2.   It shall be lawful for the fire chief or any assistant or other
person in command at a fire to require any person eighteen (18) years of age or
older to assist the department during a fire, and any such person who shall
refuse to render such assistance, when within his power to do so, shall, upon
conviction, be fined as provided in section
1-4-1  of this code. (2006 Code; amd. Ord. 1616, 2-6-2024)
4-1-9: TRAFFIC REGULATIONS DURING FIRES:
It shall be unlawful for any automobile, truck or other vehicle to pass from
behind or to follow a firetruck within five hundred feet (500') when such
firetruck is on its way to a fire or stop such vehicle within five hundred feet
(500') of any fire apparatus stopped in answer to a fire alarm. (Ord. 692, 7-7-
1952; amd. 2006 Code; Ord. 1616, 2-6-2024)
4-1-10: FIRE DEPARTMENT EQUIPMENT:
   A.   Unlawful Use Of Equipment: Whoever shall use any fire engine, hose,
cart, or any other apparatus belonging to the city for any private purpose,
other than the extinguishing of fires, or whoever shall remove the same or any
part thereof from its place of deposit, or, having the control thereof, shall
permit such engine, hose, cart, or other apparatus to be used for any private
purposes other than aforesaid, shall, upon conviction, be fined as provided in
section
1-4-1  of this code.
   B.   Damage To Equipment: Whoever shall willfully or negligently break,
deface, or in any manner injure or interfere with the use of the equipment of
the fire department shall, upon conviction, be fined as provided in section 1-
4-1 of this code. (Ord. 1616, 2-6-2024)
4-1-11:FIRE SERVICE FOR NON-RESIDENTS:
   A.   Mutual Aid Agreements: The mayor and city clerk are hereby authorized
to make and enter into agreements with corporations or organizations outside of
the city limits under the terms of which compensation in an adequate amount
shall be paid for services rendered by the fire department, and all such
agreements shall contain a clause that the city shall in nowise and under no
circumstances be held liable for any loss or damage by reason of its failure to
extinguish fires within the territory described in any such agreement. All such
agreements so entered into shall be submitted to the city council for approval.
All such agreements shall contain a clause permitting the termination of the
agreement upon six (6) months’ notice.
   B.   Non-Resident Billing: The following recitals, definitions, billing
procedures, fees, procedures for non- compliance, and severability sections
shall apply to all non-resident services called for by the department.
      1.   Recitals:
         a.   WHEREAS, the City of Carmi, Illinois, (the “City”) may render
firefighting and other emergency response services and supplies to non-
residents and others who by operation of law can be required to pay for
services in specific circumstances.
         b.   WHEREAS, the City Council of the City of Carmi recognizes that
the Carmi Fire Department incurs certain costs and expenses when being called
upon for motor vehicle accidents and motor vehicle fires that are recoverable
from the individual, or their insured, for both residents and non-residents
under certain circumstances.
         c.   WHEREAS Section 11-6-10 of the Illinois Municipal Code, 65ILCS 5/
11-6-10 states “(a) Municipalities may fix, charge, and collect fees not
exceeding the reasonable cost of the service for all services rendered by a
volunteer municipal fire department or a volunteer firefighter of any municipal
fire department for persons, businesses, and other entities who are not
residents of the municipality.” and “(b) The charge for any fees under
subsection (a) shall be computed at a rate not to exceed $250 per hour and not
to exceed $70 per hour per firefighter responding to a call for assistance. An
additional charge may be levied to reimburse the district for extraordinary
expenses of materials used in rendering such services.”
         d.   WHEREAS, Section 11-6-5 of the Illinois Municipal Code, 65 ILCS
5/11-6-5, permits the City, under appropriate circumstances, to “fix, charge,
and collect reasonable fees for specialized rescue services” provided by the
City.
         e.   WHEREAS, Section 11-6-6 of the Illinois Municipal Code, 65 ILCS
5/11-6-6, permits the City to “fix, charge, and collect reasonable fees for
technical rescue services” provided by the City.
         f.   WHEREAS, the Hazardous Material Emergency Response Reimbursement
Act, 430 ILCS 55/1 et seq., authorizes the City to recover costs incurred by
the City for an emergency response to a hazardous material emergency incident.
         g.   WHEREAS, Section 22.2 of the Environmental Protection Act, 415
ILCS 5/22.2, permits the City to recover costs incurred for removal or remedial
action as a result of a release or substantial threat of a release of a
hazardous substance or pesticide.
         h.   WHEREAS, the City renders firefighting and emergency response
services on public and private property within or outside the City’s corporate
limits to resident and non-resident persons, businesses and other entities in
the performance of its obligations to the public and the provision of such
services is costly to the City and its taxpayers.
         i.   WHEREAS, the City has or may enter into in the future mutual and/
or automatic aid intergovernmental agreements for the provision of firefighting
and emergency response services outside the corporate limits of the City.
         j.   WHEREAS, the City Council of the City of Carmi finds that it is
authorized by Illinois law and in the best interests of the City to establish a
schedule of charges for services and to charge and collect such amounts as
permitted by law.
         k.   Ordinance #461 Section 10 (a) was previously amended by Ordinance
#1416. Ordinance #1416 is hereby further amended to read as follows:
         l.   NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT ORDAINED BY THE CITY COUNCIL OF THE CITY OF
CARMI, WHITE COUNTY, ILLINOIS, AS FOLLOWS:
         m.   The City Council hereby finds that the recitals contained in the
preambles are true and correct and incorporates them into this Ordinance by
this reference.
      2.   Definitions: The following words shall have the meanings set forth
herein.
         a.   Non-resident-any person who does not permanently reside within
the boundaries of the City of Carmi, Illinois.
         b.   Resident - any person permanently residing within the City of
Carmi city limits.
         c.   Person - any individual, partnership, corporation, trust, firm,
company, estate, association, or other legal entity.
         d.   Services - including, but not limited to, requested fire
department dispatch, fire protection, fire suppression, emergency response,
motor vehicle suppression, collision or accident response, vehicle extraction,
rescue services, water recovery response, any response to spillage or release
of any hazardous materials, any threat of spillage or release of hazardous
materials, and any other situation where the Carmi Fire Department responds.
         e.   Specialized Rescue Services - includes, but is not limited to,
structural collapse, tactical rescue, high angle rescue, underwater rescue and
recovery, confined space rescue, below grade rescue, and trench rescue.
         f.   Technical Rescue Services - includes, but is not limited to,
services provided for confined space, high angle, below grade, and trench
incidents.
         g.   Careless - not taking reasonable care of, and including
disregarding the safety of others viii. Incendiary Act - An act of purposely
setting fire.
         h.   Malicious Act - An act of intentional wrongfulness without
justification or excuse.
         i.   Negligence - Acting in a careless manner, not taking steps that a
reasonable person would do.
         j.   Stand-by- Any time in which the fire department is requested or
required to be available specifically for or at an event.
         k.   False Alarm - A false report to dispatch or a firefighter of a
need for fire services.
         l.   Questionable Candidates - Persons whose circumstances surrounding
their service call may be questionable for billing under this ordinance, and a
discussion for clarity is needed for determination.
      3.   Billing Procedures: The Fire Chief or Officer in Charge at the scene
shall determine the name and address of the person receiving services at the
time services are rendered. The Fire Chief and Department Secretary shall
determine if such person(s) is a candidate for billing under this ordinance.
Questionable candidates shall be referred to the City Clerk and Mayor to
discuss the determination. Upon determination to bill, the Department Secretary
shall prepare and send an invoice for the fees and charges to the person(s)
receiving the services. All such fees and charges shall be due and payable to
the City of Carmi within thirty days of the statement date. Upon request of the
person receiving services, the Department Secretary shall arrange a payment
schedule without penalty. As may be appropriate under the circumstances, the
City shall pursue payment for services in accordance with mutual and/or
automatic aid intergovernmental agreements or state or federal law, regulation
or rule.
      4.   Fees: The fees for services provided by the Carmi Fire Department
shall be in accordance with Illinois Compiled Statutes whenever such Statutes
clearly establish fees.
         a.   Non-resident fire services shall be billed according to the
following fee schedule for each and every run the department makes for service
to any non-resident of the City of Carmi:
 
Fire Vehicle/Apparatus Charge (per hour)           $250
Volunteer Firefighter (per hour / per firefighter) $70
Foam Concentrate (per gallon)                      Billed At Current Cost
*Materials                                         Billed At Current Cost
 
         b.   *The current cost of all materials and equipment expended,
depleted, destroyed, or removed from service in accordance with NFPA Standards
and any applicable state, local, or federal laws as a result of the call.
         c.   Any person, resident or non-resident, who acts in a negligent,
careless, malicious, or incendiary manner requiring services from the Carmi
Fire Department shall be held liable to pay restitution to the City of Carmi
for services rendered according to the following fee schedule:
 
Extraction from Vehicle            $750
Extinguishing Motor Vehicle Fire   $750
Response to Incident Caused by DUI $1000
Malicious False Alarm              $500
 
         d.   After being found at fault, any person, resident or non-resident,
who requires specialized rescue services from the Carmi Fire Department shall
be held liable to pay restitution to the City of Carmi for services rendered
according to the following fee schedule:
 
Vehicle/Apparatus Charge (per vehicle / per hour  $125
Volunteer Firefighter (per hour / per firefighter $35
 
         e.   After being found at fault, any person, resident or non-resident,
who requires a hazardous materials response from the Carmi Fire Department
shall be held liable to pay restitution to the City of Carmi for services
rendered in the actual costs incurred in the course of providing emergency
action.
         f.   Fire Company stand-by requested or required for any non-city
sponsored event shall be required to make restitution to the City of Carmi for
the cost of such standby, unless such stand-by request is covered by a mutual
aid agreement.
         g.   Hourly fee time calculations shall start when the Carmi Fire
Department receives the call for dispatch, and time shall end when all vehicles
and personnel return to the fire station.
         h.   All charges shall be rounded to the next full hour.
         i.   Invoices for services shall be sent to the person(s) who received
such services and may be submitted by such person(s) to their insurance carrier
for payment via claim.
         j.   Any invoice submitted to a non-resident but not fully covered by
the insurance carrier remains the responsibility of the person(s) receiving
service.
         k.   All funds collected shall be deposited into the General Fund of
the City of Carmi.
      5.   Non-Compliance: Invoices for services which remain unpaid shall be
referred to the City Attorney for collection after a third and final notice.
Any person who fails to pay the invoice for services shall be liable for all
fees and charges due to the City and shall also pay the City’s reasonable
attorneys’ fees and expenses and costs, including, but not limited to, any
applicable court costs, incurred in collection of the amounts owed to the City.
(Ord. 745, 12-1-1958; amd. Ord. 1416, 12-7-2009, eff. 1-15-2010; Ord. 1616, 2-
6-2024)
4-1-12: ENFORCEMENT:
It shall be the duty of all officers of the fire department and all police
officers of the city to see that the provisions of this chapter are enforced
and to arrest on view any person who shall be found violating any of the
provisions of this chapter or who shall hinder, resist or refuse to obey any
such officer in the discharge of his duty, and to that end, all such officers
are hereby vested with the usual power and authority of police officers. (Ord.
1616, 2-6-2024)
CHAPTER 2
FIRE PREVENTION AND PROTECTION 1
SECTION:
4-2-1: Fireworks
4-2-2: Open Burning
4-2-3: Vented Gas Appliances
 
Notes
1 1. See subsection 9-1-1E of this code for fire prevention code.
4-2-1: FIREWORKS:
   A.   Definition: The term "fireworks" shall mean and include any explosive
composition, or any substance or combination of substances, or article prepared
for the purpose of producing a visible or audible effect of a temporary
exhibitional nature by explosion, combustion, deflagration or detonation, and
shall include blank cartridges, toy cannons in which explosives are used, the
type of balloons which require fire underneath to propel the same,
firecrackers, torpedoes, skyrockets, Roman candles, bombs, or other fireworks
of like construction, and any fireworks containing any explosive compound, or
any tablets or other device containing any explosive substance, or containing
combustible substances producing visual effects.; provided, however, that the
term "fireworks" shall not include snake or glow worm pellets; smoke devices;
sparklers; trick noisemakers known as "party poppers", "booby traps",
"snappers", "trick matches", "cigarette loads" and "auto burglar alarms"; toy
pistols, toy canes, toy guns, or other devices in which paper or plastic caps
containing twenty five hundredths (0.25) grains or less of explosive compound
are used, provided they are so constructed that the hand cannot come in contact
with the cap when in place for the explosion, and toy pistol paper or plastic
caps which contain less than twenty five hundredths (0.25) grains of explosive
mixture, the sale and use of which shall be permitted at all times. (Ord. 682,
8-6-1951; amd. 2006 Code)
   B.   Sales And Use Of Fireworks: Except as hereinafter provided, it shall be
unlawful for any person to offer for sale, expose for sale, sell at retail, or
use or explode any fireworks within the city; provided, that the city council
shall have the power to adopt reasonable rules and regulation for the granting
of permits for supervised public display of fireworks.
   C.   Exemptions From Provisions: Nothing in this section shall be construed
to prohibit any resident wholesaler, dealer or jobber to sell at wholesale such
fireworks as are not herein prohibited; or the sale of any kind of fireworks,
provided the same are to be shipped directly out of the state; or the use of
fireworks by railroads, public utilities, public and private carriers or other
transportation agencies for signal purposes or illumination; or the sale or use
of blank cartridges for show or theater, or for signal or ceremonial purposes
in athletics or sports, or for use by military organizations. (Ord. 682, 8-6-
1951)
   D.   Enforcement:
      1.   Complaint Filed; Search Warrant: Whenever the city council has
reason to believe that any violation of this section has occurred within its
jurisdiction as prescribed in subsection B of this section and that the person
so violating this section has in his possession fireworks or combustibles, it
may file or cause to be filed a complaint in writing, verified by affidavit,
with the proper authority within the jurisdiction of which the premises to be
searched are situated, stating the facts upon which such belief is founded, the
premises to be searched, and the property to be seized and procure a search
warrant and execute the same.
      2.   Seizure Of Property: Upon the execution of such search warrant, the
person executing the same shall make due return thereof to the court issuing
the same, together with an inventory of the property so taken thereunder.
