1 1. 50 ILCS 705/1 et seq.
CHAPTER 2
GENERAL OFFENSES
SECTION:
5-2-1: Illinois Criminal Code Adopted
5-2-2: Graffiti
5-2-1: ILLINOIS CRIMINAL CODE ADOPTED:
Except insofar as the application thereof is clearly impractical or
inappropriate, in view of the context of purposes or penalty as provided, all
of the definitions, requirements, regulations, prohibitions, provisions and
sections of the Illinois criminal code, 720 Illinois Compiled Statutes 5/1-1 et
seq., as amended, are hereby adopted by the city. Any and all violations
thereof shall be considered violations of this chapter, and each such violation
shall subject the violator thereof to penalty provisions of section
1-4-1 of this code. (2006 Code)
5-2-2: GRAFFITI:
   A.   Definition: For the purpose of this subsection, "graffiti" is defined
as any sign, symbol, marking, drawing, name, initial, word, diagram, sketch,
picture, or letter, or combinations thereof, placed without the express written
permission of the owner, upon the real or personal property of said owner.
   B.   Prohibited: It shall be unlawful to place graffiti upon the property of
another, whether publicly or privately owned, real or personal.
   C.   Placement With Owner's Permission: It shall be unlawful for an owner
and/or occupant of property which is in the public view to place or give
permission to place any graffiti on said property if such graffiti incites
violence or the furtherance or proliferation of gang activity by reference to
gang or criminal activity, depicts or expresses obscenity by referring to
sexual activity, or contains defamatory material about a public or private
person or group.
   D.   Removal Required: Upon notification by the city, the owner of property
upon which graffiti has been illegally placed shall remove the graffiti within
five (5) working days of the date of notification. Failure to remove graffiti
within the specified time shall cause summary abatement of the nuisance, and
cost therefor shall be assessed to the owner.
   E.   Compensation And Restitution: The owner of the property shall be
entitled to restitution and compensation for the direct cost incurred in the
repair and restoration of his property to its previous condition from any
person convicted of the offense listed in this subsection; provided, that the
property owner submits receipts or other evidence of the costs for the removal
or repair of the graffiti; and provided further, that the court enters an order
of restitution.
   F.   Responsibility Of Parent Or Guardian:
      1.   The parent or legal guardian of a juvenile who resides with such
parent or legal guardian is liable for actual damages for the wilful or
malicious acts of such juvenile which cause injury to a person or property. The
juvenile shall be deemed to have committed the offense with the knowledge,
consent, acquiescence and permission of the parent or legal guardian in
violation of this section.
      2.   The parent or legal guardian shall be liable for the fine and
requirement of restitution or reparation imposed by a court upon a juvenile
defendant for violation of this section.
      3.   The sanctions of this subsection shall apply after said parent or
legal guardian shall have received a written notice thereof, either by
certified or registered mail, return receipt requested, or by personal service
with a certificate of personal service returned, from the police department of
the city prior to the institution of any judicial sanction or penalty.
      4.   In any action brought pursuant to the provisions of this section,
the parent or legal guardian shall be made a party defendant. (2006 Code)
CHAPTER 3
ANIMAL CONTROL
SECTION:
5-3-1: Definitions
5-3-2: Owner Responsibility
5-3-3: Impoundment
5-3-4: Redemption
5-3-5: Interference
5-3-1: DEFINITIONS:
As used in this chapter the following terms mean:
ANIMAL: A dog.
ANIMAL CONTROL AUTHORITY: The person or persons designated to enforce this
chapter.
ANIMAL SHELTER: Facility designated or recognized by the city of Carmi for the
purpose of impounding and caring for animals.
AT LARGE: A dog shall be deemed to be at large when off the property of the
owner and not under restraint.
DANGEROUS DOG: A dog that without justification attacks a person or domestic
animal causing physical injury or death, or behaves in a manner that a
reasonable person would believe poses an unjustified imminent threat of serious
injury or death to one or more persons or domestic animals.
HUMANE MANNER: Care of an animal to include, but not be limited to, adequate
heat, ventilation and sanitary shelter, wholesome food and water, consistent
with the normal requirements and feeding habits of the animal's size, species,
and breed.
NUISANCE: A dog shall be considered a nuisance if it: damages, soils, defiles,
or defecates on private property other than the owner's or on public walks and
recreation areas unless such waste is immediately removed and properly disposed
of by the owner; causes unsanitary, "dangerous", or offensive conditions;
causes a disturbance by excessive barking or other noisemaking; chases
vehicles; or molests, attacks, or interferes with persons or other domestic
animals on public property.
OWNER: A person having the right of property or custody of a dog or who keeps
or harbors a dog or knowingly permits a dog to remain on or about any premises
occupied by that person.
PERSON: Any individual, corporation, partnership, organization, or institution
commonly recognized by law as a unit.
RESTRAINT: A dog shall be considered under restraint if it is within the real
property limits of its owner or secured by a leash or lead or under the control
of a responsible person. (Ord. 1420, 5-3-2010)
5-3-2: OWNER RESPONSIBILITY:
   A.   All dogs shall be kept under restraint.
   B.   Every "dangerous" dog, as determined by the city dogcatcher, shall be
confined by its owner within a building or secure enclosure adequately capable
of restraining the animal, and ensures the public safety and shall be securely
muzzled or caged whenever off the premises of its owner.
   C.   No dog shall be allowed to cause a nuisance. The owner of every dog
shall be held responsible for every behavior of such dog under the provisions
of this chapter.
   D.   Failure to comply with the provisions of this section shall be subject
to a fine of one hundred dollars ($100.00) for a first offense, two hundred
dollars ($200.00) for a second offense within one year, four hundred dollars
($400.00) for a third offense within one year, five hundred dollars ($500.00)
for a fourth or subsequent offense within one year.
   E.   Dog owners shall ensure that their dog carries identification at all
times in the form of a microchip, tag or other means to allow easy
determination of the owners. (Ord. 1420, 5-3-2010)
5-3-3: IMPOUNDMENT:
   A.   Any dog found running at large shall be impounded by the city
dogcatcher in an animal shelter and confined in a humane manner. Immediately
upon impounding a dog, the city dogcatcher shall make every reasonable effort
to notify the owner and inform such owner of the conditions whereby custody of
the animal may be regained. Dogs not claimed by their owners within a period of
five (5) full days in which the shelter is open to the public shall become the
property of the city of Carmi.
   B.   When a dog is found running at large and its ownership is verified by
the city dogcatcher, the authority may exercise the option of serving the owner
with a notice of violation in lieu of impounding the animal.
   C.   In the event that the animal control officer finds dogs to be
suffering, it shall have the right forthwith to remove or cause to have removed
any such animals to a safe place for care at the owner's expense or to
euthanize them when necessary to prevent further suffering. Return to the owner
may be withheld until the owner shall have made full payment for all expenses
so incurred.
   D.   Disposal of an animal by any method specified herein does not relieve
the owner of liability for violations and any accrued charges. (Ord. 1420, 5-3-
2010)
5-3-4: REDEMPTION:
   A.   Any animal impounded may be redeemed by the owner thereof within five
(5) days upon payment of an impoundment fee of ten dollars ($10.00) per day,
provided that if any such animal has been impounded within the previous twenty
four (24) months, the impoundment fee shall be twenty dollars ($20.00) per day
for the second impoundment, thirty dollars ($30.00) per day for the third
impoundment and forty dollars ($40.00) per day for the fourth and each
subsequent impoundment. Payment of impoundment fees is not considered to be in
lieu of any fine, penalty, or license fees.
   B.   Any animal confined for rabies quarantine, evidence, or other purpose
may be redeemed by the owner thereof upon payment of a fee of twenty five
dollars ($25.00). (Ord. 1420, 5-3-2010)
5-3-5: INTERFERENCE:
No person shall interfere with, hinder, or molest the city dogcatcher or any
agent thereof in the performance of any duty as herein provided.
Any person violating this section shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and
shall be subject to a fine of not less than two hundred fifty dollars ($250.00)
or more than five hundred dollars ($500.00). (Ord. 1420, 5-3-2010)
TITLE 6
MOTOR VEHICLES AND TRAFFIC
CHAPTER 1
TRAFFIC CODE; GENERAL PROVISIONS
SECTION:
6-1-1: Illinois Vehicle Code Adopted
6-1-2: Stop Streets
6-1-3: Speed Limits
6-1-4: One-Way Streets
6-1-5: Driving On Main Street
6-1-6: Cleats On Tires; Vehicles Restricted
6-1-7: Weight Limits
6-1-8: Penalty
6-1-9: Engine Braking
6-1-1: ILLINOIS VEHICLE CODE ADOPTED:
Except insofar as the application thereof is clearly impractical or
inappropriate, in view of the context of purposes or penalty as provided, all
of the definitions, requirements, regulations, prohibitions, provisions and
sections of the Illinois vehicle code, 625 Illinois Compiled Statutes 5/1-100
et seq., as amended, are hereby adopted by the city. Any and all violations
thereof shall be considered violations of this title, and each such violation
shall subject the violator thereof to penalty provisions under this title if
proceeded hereunder. (2006 Code)
6-1-2: STOP STREETS:
   A.   Stop Streets Designated:
Church Street: All vehicles traveling upon Cherry Street and approaching Church
Street from either the east or west shall come to a full stop before driving
upon or across Church Street.
First Street: All vehicles traveling upon Smith Street and approaching First
Street from the west or east shall come to a full stop before driving upon or
across First Street.
Third Street: All vehicles traveling upon Fackney Street and approaching Third
Street from either the east or west shall come to a full stop before driving
upon or across Third Street. (Ord. 386, 8-3-1925; amd. 2006 Code)
   B.   Installation Of Traffic Lights: There shall be installed at the
following intersections in the city, traffic lights for the better regulation
of motor vehicle traffic on Main Street:
   Main and Church Streets
   Main and Main Cross Streets
   Main and Walnut Streets
   (Ord. 649, 4-5-1948)
   C.   Placement Of Stop Signs: Stop signs shall be placed at the following
intersections in the city, and all vehicular traffic approaching such
intersections shall stop at said stop signs prior to entering such
intersections:
Rice Street and Iris Lane: Stop signs shall be placed on the east, north and
west corners of the intersection of Rice Street and Iris Lane.
Sixth Street and Maple Street: All vehicular traffic flowing north and south on
Sixth Street shall stop at the intersection of Sixth Street and Maple Street,
before proceeding through the intersection. The effect of this provision is
that, upon its passage, the intersection of Sixth Street and Maple Street shall
become a four-way stop intersection.
Seventh Street and Smith Street: Stop signs shall be placed on the east, north,
west and south corners of the intersection of Seventh Street and Smith Street.
(Ord. 1175, 11-18-1991; amd. Ord. 1194, 5-17-1993, eff. 5-31-1993; Ord. 1260,
12-1-1997; 2006 Code)
   D.   Stop Streets; Traffic Flow Regulated:
Bohleber Drive and Abelson Drive: All vehicular traffic flowing west on
Bohleber Drive shall stop at the corner of the intersection of Bohleber Drive
and Abelson Drive.
Crebs Avenue and Conger Avenue: All vehicular traffic flowing east and west on
Crebs Avenue shall stop at the intersection of Crebs Avenue and Conger Avenue
before proceeding through the intersection. The intersection of Crebs Avenue
and Conger Avenue shall become a four-way stop intersection.
Herbert Avenue and Sixth Street: All vehicular traffic flowing east on Herbert
Avenue shall stop at the intersection of Herbert Avenue and Sixth Street before
proceeding through the intersection. The intersection of Herbert Avenue and
Sixth Street shall become a one-way stop intersection.
Illini Avenue and Commerce Street: All vehicular traffic flowing west on Illini
Avenue shall stop at the intersection of Illini Avenue and Commerce Street
before proceeding through the intersection. All vehicular traffic that meets at
the intersection of Illini Avenue and 200 Commerce Street shall stop before
proceeding through the intersection. The intersection of Illini Avenue and 200
Commerce Street shall become a four-way stop intersection.
Paint Creek Lane and Rice Street: All vehicular traffic flowing east and west
on Paint Creek Lane shall stop at the intersection of Paint Creek Lane and Rice
Street before proceeding through the intersection.
Stewart Street and Hillsdale Drive and Stewart Street and Beck Street: All
vehicular traffic flowing east and west on Stewart Street shall stop at the
intersection of Stewart Street and Hillsdale Drive to the north and Stewart
Street and Beck Street to the south, before proceeding through the
intersection. The intersection of Stewart Street and Hillsdale Drive and
Stewart Street and Beck Street shall become a four-way stop intersection.
Sycamore Street and Hillsdale Drive: All vehicular traffic flowing east or west
on Sycamore Street shall stop at the corner of the intersection of Sycamore
Street and Hillsdale Drive.
Sycamore Street and Seventh Street: All vehicular traffic flowing east or west
on Sycamore Street shall stop at the corner of the intersection of Sycamore
Street and Seventh Street.
Tar Springs Drive and Paint Creek Lane: All vehicular traffic flowing either
direction on Tar Springs Drive shall stop before proceeding on to Paint Creek
Lane.
Walnut Street and Robinson Street: All vehicular traffic flowing north and
south on Walnut Street shall stop at the intersection of Walnut Street and
Robinson Street before proceeding through the intersection. The intersection of
Walnut Street and Robinson Street shall become a four-way stop intersection.
First Street and Smith Street: All vehicular traffic flowing north and south on
First Street shall stop at the intersection of First Street and Smith Street.
The intersection of First Street and Smith Street shall become a four-way stop
intersection.
Third Street and Maple Street: All vehicular traffic flowing north and south on
Third Street shall stop at the intersection of Third Street and Maple Street
before proceeding through the intersection. The intersection of Third Street
and Maple Street shall become a four-way stop intersection.
Third Street and Shipley Street: All vehicular traffic flowing north and south
on Third Street shall stop at the intersection of Third Street and Shipley
Street before proceeding through the intersection. The intersection of Third
Street and Shipley Street shall become a four-way stop intersection.
Seventh Street and Maple Street: All vehicular traffic flowing north and south
on Seventh Street shall stop at the intersection of Seventh Street and Maple
Street before proceeding through the intersection.
Ninth Street and Maple Street: All vehicular traffic flowing north and south on
Ninth Street shall stop at the intersection of Ninth Street and Maple Street
before proceeding through the intersection. All vehicular traffic flowing west
on Maple Street shall stop at the intersection of Ninth Street and Maple Street
before proceeding through the intersection. (Ord. 1254, 8-18-1997; amd. Ord.
1255, 8-18-1997; Ord. 1256, 10-6-1997; Ord. 1257, 10-6-1997; Ord. 1276, 3-29-
1999; Ord. 1287, 11-1-1999; Ord. 1299, 12-18-2000; 2006 Code; Ord. 1371, 2-20-
2007; Ord. 1372, 2-20-2007; Ord. 1402, 1-5-2009; Ord. 1442, 8-22-2011; Ord.
1443, 8-22-2011; Ord. 1454, 6-11-2012; Ord. 1469, 9-3-2013)
6-1-3: SPEED LIMITS:
   A.   Due Care Requirement: No vehicle shall be driven upon any street or
alley of the City at a speed which is greater than is reasonable and proper
with regard to traffic conditions and the use of the street or alley, or
endangers the safety of any person or property. The fact that the speed of a
vehicle does not exceed the applicable maximum speed limit does not relieve the
driver from the duty to decrease speed when approaching and crossing an
intersection, approaching and going around a curve, when approaching a hill
crest, when traveling upon any narrow or winding street or alley or where
special hazards exist with respect to pedestrians or other traffic or by reason
of weather or street or alley conditions. Speed must be decreased as may be
necessary to avoid colliding with any person or vehicle on or entering the
street or alley in compliance with legal requirements and the duty of all
persons to use due care.
   B.   Specific Streets:
      1.   Generally:
Streets And Alleys Maximum Speed Limits
Streets And Alleys                     Maximum Speed Limits
Alleys                                 15 miles per hour
Church Street south of Ratcliff Street 30 miles per hour
Commerce Street                        35 miles per hour
Fairground Road                        30 miles per hour
Main Street                            As posted from time to time by the State
                                       of Illinois
Oak Street                             As posted from time to time by the State
                                       of Illinois
Streets, alleys, and roadways within
Bradshaw Park, Burrell Woods and all   10 miles per hour
other City owned or maintained parks
 
   C.   Other Streets: Except as provided in subsection B of this section,
maximum speed limits for vehicles on all streets in the City shall be twenty
five (25) miles per hour.
   D.   Definitions:
    ALLEY: For purposes of this section the term "alley" shall mean, a public
way within a block, generally giving access to the rear of lots or buildings
and not used for general traffic circulation.
   STREET: For purposes of this section the term "street" shall mean, the
entire width between boundary lines of every way publicly maintained where any
part thereof is open to the use of the public for purposes of vehicle travel.
   VEHICLE: For purposes of this section the term "vehicle" shall mean, every
device, in, upon or by which any person or property is or may be transported or
drawn upon a street or alley, except devices moved by human power and devices
used exclusively upon stationary rails or tracts. (Ord. 1486, 6-2-2015, eff. 6-
9-2015)

streets with traffic flowing as follows: (Ord. 1493, 12-1-2015, eff. 1-4-2016)

6-1-5: DRIVING ON MAIN STREET:
   A.   Lincoln School Crosswalk:
      1.   U.S. Route 460: All motor vehicles traveling on or along U.S. Route
460 (SBI 14) in the City shall stop at the Lincoln School crosswalk when the
red lens of the school crossing signal located at such crosswalk is illuminated
by rapid intermittent flashes; and after such red signal ceases, such vehicles
shall proceed across said crosswalk with caution and only after allowing the
right-of-way to all pedestrians using said crosswalk. It shall be unlawful for
any person to violate the provisions of this subsection.
      2.   State Route 1: All motor vehicles traveling on or along Illinois
State Route 1 (SBI 1) in the City shall stop at the Lincoln School crosswalk
when the red lens of the school crossing signal located at such crosswalk is
illuminated by rapid intermittent flashes; and after such red signal ceases,
such vehicles shall proceed across said crosswalk with caution and only after
allowing the right-of-way to all pedestrians using said crosswalk.
      3.   Location:
         a.   The Lincoln School crosswalk on said U.S. Route 460 is located
approximately at the intersection of Tenth Street and U.S. Route 460 in the
City and shall be plainly marked by two (2) white lines indicating the
boundaries and location of said crosswalk.
         b.   The Lincoln School crosswalk on Illinois State Route 1 is located
approximately at the intersection of Ninth Street and Illinois State Route 1 in
the City and shall be plainly marked by two (2) white lines indicating the
boundaries and location of said crosswalk. (Ord. 878, 8-6-1973; amd. 2006 Code)
   B.   Washington Grade School Crossing:
      1.   Stop At Crossing Required: All persons driving motor vehicles on and
along Main Street (Routes 1 and 460) in the City shall stop at the Washington
Grade School crosswalk when the red lens of the school crossing signal located
at such crosswalk is illuminated by rapid intermittent flashes; and thereafter,
such persons driving motor vehicles as aforesaid shall drive across said
crosswalk with caution and only after allowing the right-of- way to pedestrians
using said crosswalk. It shall be unlawful for any person to violate the
provisions of this subsection.
      2.   Location: Said crosswalk crosses Main Street at a point on Main
Street directly in front of the center front door of the Washington Grade
School, and shall be plainly marked by two (2) white lines indicating the
boundaries and location of said crosswalk. (Ord. 879, 8-6-1973; amd. 2006 Code)
6-1-6: CLEATS ON TIRES; VEHICLES RESTRICTED:
It shall be unlawful for any person to drive any tractor or other vehicle with
cleats or other projections on the wheels thereof on any of the paved streets
of the City without first removing said cleats or projections or laying down a
plank at least eight inches (8") wide and two inches (2") thick over which said
tractor or vehicle may be driven. (Ord. 364, 11-5-1923; amd. 2006 Code)
6-1-7: WEIGHT LIMITS:
It shall be unlawful for any person to haul over any earth or gravel street or
alley within the corporate limits of the City at any time when the ground is
thawing or, by reason of wet weather, is in condition to be cut up and injured
by heavy hauling, a load on any vehicle with tires of less than three inches
(3") in width, the combined weight of which loaded vehicle, including the
driver, shall be more than two thousand five hundred (2,500) pounds; or any
vehicle with tires of three inches (3") and less than four inches (4") in
width, the combined weight of which load, vehicle and driver shall be more than
three thousand (3,000) pounds; or on any vehicle with tires of four inches (4")
and less than five inches (5") in width, the combined weight of which load,
vehicle and driver shall be more than three thousand five hundred (3,500)
pounds; or on any vehicle with tires of five inches (5") or more in width, the
combined weight of which load, vehicle and driver shall be more than three
thousand eight hundred (3,800) pounds. (Ord. 390, 2-1-1926; amd. 2006 Code)
6-1-8: PENALTY:
Any person violating any provision of this title shall be punishable as
provided in section
1-4-1 of this Code. (2006 Code)
6-1-9: ENGINE BRAKING:
   A.   It shall be unlawful to operate or activate any engine braking system,
aka "jake brake", that emits excessive noise.
   B.   Any person who violates any provision of this section is guilty of a
misdemeanor and upon conviction thereof shall be punished by a fine of not less
than seventy five dollars ($75.00) nor more than two hundred dollars ($200.00)
for each offense. (Ord. 1412, 8-18-2009)
CHAPTER 2
PARKING REGULATIONS
SECTION:
6-2-1: Miscellaneous Parking Restrictions
6-2-2: Parking In Alleys
6-2-3: Parking Near First Presbyterian Church
6-2-4: Diagonal Or Parallel Parking
6-2-5: Truck Or Tractor Parking Restricted
6-2-6: Time Limit Parking Restrictions
6-2-7: No Parking Areas Designated
6-2-1: MISCELLANEOUS PARKING RESTRICTIONS:
   A.   Fireplugs; No Parking Zones: It shall be unlawful for any person to
park a motor vehicle within fifteen feet (15') of any fireplug in the city, or
in any no parking zone on the streets in the city, as designated by yellow
lines on streets and curbs. (Ord. 487, 6-3-1941; amd. 2006 Code)
   B.   Fire Stations; Alarms Of Fire:
      1.   Fire Station Doorways: It shall be unlawful to park any vehicle
within twenty feet (20') of the driveway entrance to any fire station and on
the side of a street opposite the entrance to any fire station within seventy
five feet (75') of such entrance (when properly signposted).
      2.   Fire Alarm; Duty Of Drivers: In all cases where a fire alarm is
sounded, it shall be the duty of all persons having automobiles, trucks, or
vehicles of any kind in or upon the streets of the city to immediately drive or
move the same to the curb and remain there until fire department engines all
have passed. (Ord. 916, 5-3-1976; amd. 2006 Code)
   C.   Main Street Parking During Corn Days:
      1.   During Carmi's annual fall festival, Corn Days, parking of all
vehicles shall be prohibited on Main Street from Main Cross Street to Jessup
Street. Through traffic shall be diverted from this area by barricades, and
signage in accordance with Illinois department of transportation regulations.
      2.   During the annual fall festival, Corn Days, vehicular access to Main
Street from Main Cross Street to Jessup Street will be restricted and
notification of such restriction will be made by placement of barricades and
appropriate signage.
      3.   Permission of the Carmi chief of police or his designee will be
required for vehicular entry into this area during the annual fall festival,
Corn Days. Nothing herein shall be construed to deny access to this area by
emergency vehicles in the performance of their duties.
      4.   Any person who violates any provision of this subsection is guilty
of a misdemeanor and upon conviction thereof shall be punished by a fine of not
less than seventy five dollars ($75.00) nor more than two hundred dollars
($200.00) for each offense. (Ord. 1411, 8-18-2009)
6-2-2: PARKING IN ALLEYS:
   A.   Prohibition; Exceptions: No person shall park a motor vehicle upon any
alley right of way within the corporate limits of the city, with the following
exceptions:
      1.   Persons may park motor vehicles upon the alley rights of way within
the corporate limits of the city for a period of time not to exceed fifteen
(15) minutes for the purpose of loading or unloading the vehicles.
      2.   Persons may park motor vehicles upon the alley rights of way within
the corporate limits of the city for a period of time in excess of fifteen (15)
minutes upon twenty four (24) hours' notice to corporate authorities and city
police, and upon written permission from the corporate authorities, except
twenty four (24) hours' prior notice shall not be required in cases of
emergencies.
   B.   Towing Illegally Parked Vehicles: Any motor vehicle parked upon an
alley right of way within the corporate limits of the city, which restricts the
use of the alley by any emergency vehicles, including, but not limited to,
firetrucks, ambulances and police cars, shall be towed or removed from the
right-of-way at the vehicle owner's risk, cost, expense and liability. (Ord.
1080, 9-18-1984; amd. 2006 Code)
6-2-3: PARKING NEAR FIRST PRESBYTERIAN CHURCH:
   A.   No Parking Any Time:
      1.   There shall be no parking of vehicles at any time on the westerly
side of First Street from a point beginning where the northerly side of Stewart
Street is extended in an easterly direction, intersects with the westerly side
of First Street, thence northerly along the westerly side a distance of one
hundred twenty five feet (125').
      2.   No vehicles shall be parked on the easterly side of First Street
lying between Stewart Street and Smith Street in an area being fifteen feet
(15') southerly and fifteen feet (15') northerly of a point on First Street due
west of the southwesterly corner of the First Presbyterian Church of Carmi
property.
   B.   Parking Allowed During Special Functions:
      1.   There shall be no parking of vehicles at any time on the westerly
side of First Street lying between Stewart Street and Smith Street, except
between the hours of eight thirty o'clock (8:30) A.M. to twelve thirty o'clock
(12:30) P.M. on Sundays, and during times when the First Presbyterian Church of
Carmi is having special meetings, funerals, weddings, and other special church
functions, not to exceed twenty five (25) times per year; provided, however,
there shall be no parking of vehicles at any time on the area described in
subsection A1 of this section.
      2.   The First Presbyterian Church of Carmi shall notify the Police
Department, in advance, of the dates and times of special meetings, funerals,
weddings, and other special church functions. (Ord. 1185, 9-8-1992; amd. 2006
Code)
6-2-4: DIAGONAL OR PARALLEL PARKING:
   A.   Main Street:
      1.   Parallel Parking: It shall be unlawful to stand or park any vehicle
other than parallel with the curb and with the vehicle within twelve inches
(12") of the regularly established curb line on Main Street, as follows:
Between Jessup Street and Main Cross Street, within three (3) blocks on Main
Street, on both sides thereof.
Between Fifth Street and Locust Street. (Ord. 653, 6-7-1948, eff. 7-1-1948;
amd. Ord. 772, 7-31-1961; 2006 Code)
      2.   Projecting Beyond Parking Line: It shall be unlawful for any person
to park any motor vehicle on Main Street in such a manner that it projects
beyond the back line or front line for parking marked on said street. (Ord.
487, 6-3-1941; amd. 2006 Code)
   B.   Main Cross Street:
      1.   Parallel Parking Required: The diagonal parking of motor vehicles on
Main Cross Street between Cherry Street and Main Street, in the City, shall be
prohibited, and all such vehicles parked on Main Cross Street as designated
shall be parked parallel with Main Cross Street as designated on either side
thereof. It shall be unlawful for any person to park a motor vehicle on said
portion of said Main Cross Street in violation of this subsection B1.
      2.   Additional Provision: This subsection shall be deemed to be in
addition to and not in conflict with nor a repeal of prior or existing
ordinances of the City, but shall supplement the provisions of other existing
ordinances regulating the parking of motor vehicles in the City. (Ord. 688, 4-
2-1952; amd. 2006 Code)
6-2-5: TRUCK OR TRACTOR PARKING RESTRICTED:
   A.   Parking Time Limit: No person shall stand or park a tractor, semi, and
semi-trailer, vehicle classified over one (1) ton, trailer, float or bus in any
street in the City of Carmi for a longer period than three (3) continuous
hours.
   B.   Leaving With Engine Running: No person shall cause or permit a truck,
tractor, semi, semi-trailer, vehicle classified over one (1) ton, trailer,
float or bus to idle with any engine running in the City of Carmi unless such
truck, tractor, semi, semi-trailer, vehicle classified over one (1) ton,
trailer, float or bus is personally attended by the driver thereof, unless such
vehicle is in the process of being loaded or unloaded. For purposes of this
section, "personally attended by the driver thereof" shall mean the driver
shall be personally inside or on such truck, tractor, semi, semi-trailer,
vehicle classified over one (1) ton, trailer, float or bus or be personally
present upon the street or ground in the immediate vicinity where such truck,
tractor, semi, semi- trailer, vehicle classified over one (1) ton, trailer,
float or bus is parked, other than in a residence, store or other building in
the vicinity where truck, tractor, semi, semi-trailer, vehicle classified over
one (1) ton, trailer, float or bus is parked.
   C.   Nuisance; Abatement By Police: Any vehicle parked in violation of this
section is hereby declared to be a nuisance which may be abated by any police
officer removing or having removed such vehicle to any authorized garage, and
the costs of removal shall constitute a lien upon said vehicle. (Ord. 1502, 5-
3-2016, eff. 6-8-2016)
6-2-6: TIME LIMIT PARKING RESTRICTIONS:
   A.   Miscellaneous:
Main Street: Parking of all vehicles shall be prohibited and it shall be
unlawful to permit any vehicle to stand or park along and upon the corporate
limits of Main Street from twelve o'clock (12:00) midnight to five o'clock (5:
00) A.M. every day. (Ord. 1331, 5-19-2003)
   B.   Ten Minute Parking:
U.S. Post Office: It shall be unlawful for any person to park for more than ten
(10) minutes any motor driven vehicle, or any tractor, engine, or any
conveyance of any kind or character upon or along the east side of Walnut
Street and in front of the property occupied by the U.S. Post Office between
the hours of six o'clock (6:00) A.M. and six o'clock (6:00) P.M. of each and
every day, except Sunday. (Ord. 469, 10-3-1938; amd. 2006 Code)
   C.   Fifteen Minute Parking:
South Jessup Street: The east and west sides of South Jessup Street shall be a
loading/unloading zone only with a fifteen (15) minute time limit. (Ord. 1494,
12-1-2015, eff. 1-4-2016)
   D.   Thirty Minute Parking:
Walnut Street: It shall be unlawful for vehicles to park for a length of time
longer than thirty (30) minutes on the south half of the west side of Walnut
Street lying between Main Street and Robinson Street in the City, between the
hours of seven o'clock (7:00) A.M. and five o'clock (5:00) P.M. Central
Standard Time. (Ord. 1125, 1-18-1988; amd. 2006 Code; Ord. 1494, 12-1-2015,
eff. 1-4-2016)

CHAPTER 3
BICYCLES
SECTION:
6-3-1: Registration Requirements
6-3-2: Operation Of Bicycles; Equipment Requirements
6-3-3: Violation; Penalty
6-3-1: REGISTRATION REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   Registration Required:
      1.   Any person who owns a bicycle or bicycles within the corporate
limits of the city shall register the bicycle(s) with the police department;
said registry shall be excepted from any person, business or corporation which
has bicycle(s) on its premises for repair or sale.
      2.   The police department will not take a theft report of a bicycle
unless the bicycle has previously been registered.
   B.   Hours And Fee: The registration shall be between the hours of eight
o'clock (8:00) A.M. and four o'clock (4:00) P.M., Monday through Friday,
excluding holidays. The registration fee is one dollar ($1.00) and shall be due
upon registration.
   C.   Registration Tag: Any person who is a resident of the city who is
riding, possessing, transporting, or carrying a bicycle shall have a
registration sticker/tag that has been previously issued by the police
department affixed to the bicycle, and visible at all times to a police officer
or the officer's agent.
   D.   Proof Of Registration: When requested by a police officer, or the
officer's agent, any person in possession of a bicycle shall provide proof of
registration.
   E.   Improper Or Missing Registration:
      1.   Impoundment Of Bicycles: Any bicycle with a defaced, missing, or
altered registration shall be subject to seizure by the police department.
      2.   Reregistration: The owner of any bicycle with a defaced, missing, or
altered registration shall immediately reregister the bicycle with the police
department.
   F.   Change Of Ownership: After the initial registration, any person who
resides within the city and assumes ownership of a bicycle by purchase, trade
or transfer of ownership shall, within ten (10) days, register the bicycle with
the police department. (Ord. 1334, 9-2-2003)
6-3-2: OPERATION OF BICYCLES; EQUIPMENT REQUIREMENTS:
All rules and regulations that are applicable in the Illinois vehicle code, 625
Illinois Compiled Statutes 5/11-1501 through 5/11-1515, shall be enforced as
part of this chapter. (Ord. 1334, 9-2-2003)
6-3-3: VIOLATION; PENALTY:
Any person violating any of the provisions of this chapter shall, upon
conviction thereof, be fined not less than ten dollars ($10.00) nor more than
fifty dollars ($50.00) for each offense. Any person who is convicted of a
violation of any provision of this chapter for a third time shall be guilty of
a class C misdemeanor. (Ord. 1334, 9-2-2003)
CHAPTER 4
ABANDONED, INOPERABLE VEHICLES
SECTION:
6-4-1: Definitions
6-4-2: Abandonment Of Vehicles
6-4-3: Leaving Vehicles On Street
6-4-4: Inoperable Vehicles Declared A Nuisance
6-4-5: Disposal Of Inoperable Vehicles
6-4-1: DEFINITIONS:
The following definitions shall apply in the interpretation and enforcement of
this chapter:
ABANDONED VEHICLE: Any vehicle which is left on any street, highway, or
property for such time and under such circumstances as to cause such vehicle
reasonably to appear to have been abandoned.
INOPERABLE MOTOR VEHICLE: A. Any motor vehicle, whether on public or private
property and in view of the general public, from which, for a period of at
least seven (7) days, the engine, wheels or other parts have been removed, or
on which the engine, wheels or other parts have been altered, damaged, or
otherwise so treated that the vehicle is incapable of being driven under its
own motor power.
   B.   "Inoperable motor vehicle" shall not include a motor vehicle which has
been rendered temporarily incapable of being driven under its own power in
order to perform ordinary service or repair operations nor to any motor
vehicles that are kept within a building when not in use, to historic vehicles
over twenty five (25) years of age, or to a motor vehicle on the premises of a
place of business engaged in wrecking or junking of motor vehicles.
PERSON: Any person, firm, partnership, association, corporation, company, or
other organization of any kind.
PROPERTY: Any real property within the city which is not a street or highway.
STREET OR HIGHWAY: The entire width between the boundary lines of every way
publicly maintained when any part thereof is open to use of the public for
purposes of vehicular travel.
VEHICLE: A machine propelled by power other than human power designed to travel
along the ground by use of wheels, treads, runners, or slides and transport
persons or property or pull machinery and shall include, without limitation,
automobile, truck, trailer, motorcycle, tractor, buggy and wagon. (Ord. 1197,
7-19-1993)
6-4-2: ABANDONMENT OF VEHICLES:
No person shall abandon any vehicle within the city and no person shall leave
any vehicle at any place within the city, whether on public or private
property, for such time and under such circumstances as to cause such vehicle
reasonably to appear to have been abandoned. (Ord. 1197, 7-19-1993)
6-4-3: LEAVING VEHICLES ON STREET:
No person shall leave any partially dismantled, nonoperating, wrecked, or
junked vehicle on any street, highway, or property within the city. (Ord. 1197,
7-19-1993)
6-4-4: INOPERABLE VEHICLES DECLARED A NUISANCE:
"Inoperable motor vehicles", as defined in section
6-4-1 of this chapter, whether on public or private property, are hereby
declared to be a nuisance. (Ord. 1197, 7-19-1993)
6-4-5: DISPOSAL OF INOPERABLE VEHICLES:
   A.   Disposal Required; Notice From City: All persons are required to
dispose of any inoperable motor vehicles under their control within seven (7)
days upon written notice received from the corporate authorities or from the
chief of police or any member of his department designated by him commanding
such disposition of said inoperable motor vehicle.
   B.   Disposal By City: If, after the seven (7) days' notice has expired, the
owner has not disposed of said inoperable motor vehicle under his control, then
the chief of police or any member of his department may remove any inoperable
motor vehicle or parts thereof. (Ord. 1197, 7-19-1993)
CHAPTER 5
IMPOUNDMENT OF MOTOR VEHICLES
SECTION:
6-5-1: Definitions
6-5-2: Violations Authorizing Impoundment
6-5-3: Seizure And Impoundment
6-5-4: Administrative Hearing
6-5-5: Disposition Of Impounded Motor Vehicle
6-5-6: Motor Vehicle Possession
6-5-7: Towing Agency
6-5-8: Refund Of Administrative Fee
6-5-1: DEFINITIONS:
BUSINESS DAY: Any day in which the offices of city hall are open to the public
for a minimum of seven (7) hours.
LEVEL 1 ADMINISTRATIVE FEE: Two hundred dollars ($200.00).
LEVEL 2 ADMINISTRATIVE FEE: One hundred dollars ($100.00).
MOTOR VEHICLE: Every vehicle which is self-propelled, including, but not
limited to, automobiles, trucks, vans, motorcycles, and motor scooters.
OWNER OF RECORD: The record titleholder(s) of the motor vehicle as registered
with the secretary of state, state of Illinois; or if not registered in
Illinois, the particular state where the motor vehicle is registered. (Ord.
1440, 7-18-2011)
6-5-2: VIOLATIONS AUTHORIZING IMPOUNDMENT:
   A.   Any motor vehicle, operated with the express or implied permission of
the owner of record, that is used in connection with the following violations,
shall be subject to seizure and impoundment by the city, and the owner of
record of said motor vehicle shall be liable to the city for a level 1
administrative fee, as provided for in this chapter, in addition to any towing
and storage fees as hereinafter provided.
State Statute Violations
State Statute       Violations
625 ILCS 5/6-303    Driving while license revoked
625 ILCS 5/11-204   Fleeing or attempting to elude a peace officer
625 ILCS 5/11-501   Driving under the influence of alcohol/drugs
625 ILCS 5/11-503   Reckless driving or aggravated reckless driving
625 ILCS 5/11-506   Street racing
625 ILCS 5/11-601.5 Speeding in excess of 40 mph class A misdemeanor

720 ILCS 5/18-1     Robbery
720 ILCS 5/18-2     Armed robbery
